فهذه جملة المباحث المتوجهة على هذا الدليل [ والله أعلم) ]
والجواب : إن بديهة العقل حاكمة : بأن الموجود . إما واجب لذاته ، أو ممكن لذاته . والبديهة حاكمة : بأن الواجب لذاته ، لا يقبل العدم [ والبديهة شاهدة : بأن ذلك الواجب لذاته. إما أن يكون مختاراً ، أو موجباً (۳) ) والبديهة حاكمة : بأن الممكن لذاته، لا بد وأن ينتهي إلى الواجب لذاته ، إما بغير واسطة ، أو بواسطة واحدة ، أو بوسائط كثيرة . ثم إن (4) ] البديهة شاهدة : بأن معلول الواجب لذاته ، لا بد وأن يدوم بدوام تلك العلة ، وحيث لم يكن ذلك المؤثر [ موجباً () ] وإذا بطل هذا ثبت أن المؤثر فاعل مختار . والبديهة شاهدة : بأن كل ما كان فعلا لفاعل [ مختار (۱) ] فهو محدث. فيثبت بهذا : أن كل ما صح العدم عليه . فالقديم وجب أن لا يصح [ عليه (۷) ] العدم . وما ذكر تموه من السؤالات جارى مجرى القدح في الضروريات . فلا يلتفت إليه
[ والله أعلم (٨) ]
It was existent - not from a cause. This is an obscure question. The second question: that we say: If the possible existent must have a cause, then the possible non-existence also must have a cause. So the non-existence of the world in eternity, and the non-existence of God (Exalted) in eternity, must have a cause. And the mentioned division applies to it, etc. The third question: If the world were originated, its origination would be specific to a particular time. The agent who specified its bringing into existence at that specific time, if it is impossible for him to bring it into existence at another time, then he is a necessitator by essence, not a free agent. Then from his being a necessitator by essence follows the eternity of the world. But if it is permissible for that agent to bring the world into existence at that time or at another time instead, then either that preference depends on a preponderator or not. The first is false, for the discussion about the specification of that time with that preponderator is like the discussion about its specification with that originated thing, and the demand returns in the same way, leading to infinite regress. So the second division remains, which is that the specification of that time with this effect is a preponderance without a preponderator. So we say: If this is permissible, why is it not also permissible that the eternal thing cease to exist after its existence without a preponderator or a specificator? For neither of the two cases is more obviously impossible and corrupt in the intellect than the other. The fourth question: We grant that if that eternal thing were to cease after its existence, it must have a preponderator. So why is it not permissible that that preponderator be capable? His saying: 'Everything that is an act of a free agent is originated' – we say: This is countered by the many points mentioned in the explanation that the dependence of the effect on the cause is not conditional upon origination. The fifth question: We grant that that cause is necessitating; but why does its perpetuity necessitate the perpetuity of the effect? Its explanation: The existing cause is not far from its effect being dependent on a privative condition—do you not see that weight necessitates the descent of the heavy, conditioned upon the absence of a chain preventing descent, and you permit that in the eternal non-existence it may cease? If this is established, we say: Why is it not permissible to say that the existent necessary in itself was a cause for the existence of that eternal thing, except that that effect was conditioned upon an eternal privative condition, then that eternal privative condition ceased, so necessarily that effect ceased. These are the total points of discussion directed against this proof (and God knows best). The answer: Verily the intuition of reason judges that the existent is either necessary in itself or possible in itself. And the intuition judges that the necessary in itself does not admit non-existence. And the intuition testifies that that necessary in itself is either free or necessitating. And the intuition judges that the possible in itself must terminate at the necessary in itself, either without intermediary or with one intermediary or many intermediaries. Then the intuition testifies that the effect of the necessary in itself must remain as long as that cause remains. And when that cause is not necessitating, then if this is false, it is established that the cause is a free agent. And the intuition testifies that everything that is an act of a free agent is originated. Thus it is established: everything that non-existence is valid for—the eternal must not have non-existence valid for it. And what you have mentioned of questions are in the manner of impugning necessary truths, so no attention is paid to it. (And God knows best).
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage presents five objections (the second through fifth) to a proof (likely the proof of the world's temporal origination from the principle of specification), followed by a comprehensive answer. The objections raise difficulties: the second question argues that if possible beings need a cause, then possible non-being also needs a cause, so the non-existence of the world before creation would need a cause. The third question addresses the problem of specification: if the world originated at a specific time, either the agent was necessitated (making the world eternal) or had a choice; if choice, the preference either requires a preponderator (leading to infinite regress) or is a preponderance without a preponderator, which the objector says would allow the eternal to cease without cause. The fourth question concedes that cessation requires a cause but asks why that cause cannot be a capable agent (qādir), and counters the claim that every act of a free agent is originated by noting that the connection between cause and effect is not conditional upon origination. The fifth question concedes a necessitating cause but argues that its effect may depend on a privative condition that can cease, allowing the effect to perish. The answer then invokes the self-evident intuitions (badīha) of reason: every existent is either necessary in itself (wājib li-dhātihi) or possible in itself (mumkin li-dhātihi); the necessary cannot admit non-existence; the necessary is either free or necessitating; the possible must terminate in the necessary; the effect of a necessary cause must endure as long as the cause; if the cause is not necessitating, it is free; every act of a free agent is originated (muḥdath). Thus, whatever admits non-existence is originated, and the eternal does not admit non-existence. The objections are dismissed as attempts to impugn necessary truths and are to be ignored.

Misconception: That the specification of a time for the world's creation disproves its creation.
Correction: Al-Razi will answer this with self-evident truths, showing that the objections are not decisive.

Checkpoint
In the third objection, what does the objector claim follows if the agent is necessitated (على أنه موجب بالذات)?
A) The world is originated at that time.
B) The world must be eternal.
C) The agent has free will.
D) The preponderator is unnecessary.

Key Takeaway
The four objections raise deep puzzles about causation, time, and agency, but they are presented as challenges that require a foundational answer.

?
Have you ever demanded that God explain His timing in your life? When you face a trial, do you secretly believe that a delay in relief means God is arbitrary? How does this lesson challenge your impatience with His decree?
?
If you truly believe that God's will is not bound by external preponderators, do you live with the confidence that His choices are wise even when they seem inexplicable? Or do you try to rationalize His actions to make yourself comfortable?
?
Consider the possibility that your own existence depends on a privative condition—something's absence that could cease. Does that thought make you cling more tightly to the Creator who alone is necessary? How can you cultivate that dependence today?

The Self-Evident Rational Answer
Al-Razi presents a series of self-evident rational judgments that settle the debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi uses a series of self-evident rational judgments (badīha) to settle the objections and establish the world's temporal origination.

Core Idea
Self-evident truths of reason form the foundation that dispels all speculative objections.

Al-Razi now delivers his answer by invoking the foundational truths that every rational person must acknowledge. These self-evident judgments (badīha) about existence, necessity, possibility, and causation provide the definitive response to the earlier objections. In this passage, we see the core of his theological epistemology: the appeal to necessary truths of reason.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer passage
Read the Arabic passage from 'والجواب' to the end, then the translation. Notice the repeated use of 'البديهة' (intuition).
This section is dense with claims; read slowly.
2
Identify the series of self-evident judgments
Al-Razi lists several judgments: every existent is either necessary or possible; the necessary does not admit non-existence; the necessary is either free or necessitating; the possible must terminate with the necessary; the effect of the necessary remains as long as the cause; if the cause is not necessitating, it is free; every act of a free agent is originated.
Write each judgment down.
3
Understand how each judgment refutes the objections
For example, the judgment that the necessary cannot cease to exist directly answers the third objection about the eternal ceasing. The judgment that the effect of the necessary remains with the cause refutes the fifth objection's privative condition argument.
4
Recognize the dismissal strategy
Al-Razi concludes by saying the objections are like impugning necessary truths and should be ignored. This shows his confidence in the self-evident foundation.

Causality and Created Things
intermediate

Fifth Objection: Privation Conditions and Persistence of Effects
Presents the fifth objection using the example of gravity and a privative condition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fifth objection against the proof for a free creator, which argues that a necessitating agent's effect may depend on a privative condition and thus need not be perpetual.

Core Idea
Causality may be conditioned on the absence of hindrances.

The objector concedes that the agent is a necessitator but argues that its effect may not be perpetual if a privative condition—like the absence of a chain—is removed. This challenges the proof that a perpetual cause must have a perpetual effect. The passage presents this objection with a clear example.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic objection passage once, then its translation. Notice how the objector concedes the point but introduces a new condition.
The key phrase is 'شرط عدمي' (privative condition).
2
Understand the gravity analogy
The objector uses the example of gravity (ثقل) causing descent only if there is no chain. This illustrates how a cause's effect can be conditional.
This analogy is central to the objection.
3
Identify the argument structure
The objection has four parts: concession, explanation (privative condition), example (gravity), and application to the divine case.
Look for the phrase 'فنقول' which introduces the application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السؤال الخامس : سلمنا أن ذلك المؤثر موجب ، فلم يلزم من دوامه دوام المعلول ؟ بيانه : أن المؤثر الموجود لا يبعد أن يتوقف تأثيره في معلوله على شرط عدمي ألا ترى أن الثقل يوجب نزول الثقيل، بشرط عدم السلسلة العائقة عن النزول ، وأنتم جوزتم في العدم الأزلي : أن يزول . وإذا ثبت هذا ، فنقول : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : الموجود الواجب لذاته ، كان علة لوجود ذلك القديم، إلا أن ذلك التأثير ، كان مشروطاً بشرط عدمي أزلي . ثم إن ذلك الشرط العدمي الأزلي ، قد زاله . فلا جرم زال ذلك المعلول . فهذه جملة المباحث المتوجهة على هذا الدليل والله أعلم .
والجواب : إن بديهة العقل حاكمة : بأن الموجود إما واجب لذاته ، أو ممكن لذاته . والبديهة حاكمة : بأن الواجب لذاته ، لا يقبل العدم . والبديهة شاهدة : بأن ذلك الواجب لذاته إما أن يكون مختاراً ، أو موجباً . والبديهة حاكمة : بأن الممكن لذاته، لا بد وأن ينتهي إلى الواجب لذاته ، إما بغير واسطة ، أو بواسطة واحدة ، أو بوسائط كثيرة . ثم إن البديهة شاهدة : بأن معلول الواجب لذاته ، لا بد وأن يدوم بدوام تلك العلة ، وحيث لم يكن ذلك المؤثر موجباً . وإذا بطل هذا ثبت أن المؤثر فاعل مختار . والبديهة شاهدة : بأن كل ما كان فعلاً لفاعل مختار فهو محدث. فيثبت بهذا : أن كل ما صح العدم عليه فالقديم وجب أن لا يصح عليه العدم . وما ذكرتموه من السؤالات جار مجرى القدح في الضروريات . فلا يلتفت إليه والله أعلم .
The fifth question: We concede that that agent is a necessitator, but why does its perpetuity necessitate the perpetuity of the effect? Its explanation: the existing agent is not far from its effect depending on a privative condition; do you not see that gravity necessitates the descent of the heavy object, on condition of the absence of a chain preventing descent, and you have allowed in eternal non-existence that it cease. And if this is established, we say: why is it not permissible to say that the existing necessary in itself was a cause for the existence of that eternal, except that that influence was conditioned by an eternal privative condition. Then that eternal privative condition has ceased. So inevitably that effect ceased. So this is the sum of the objections directed at this proof – and God knows best. And the answer: The intuition of reason (badīhat al-ʿaql) judges that the existent is either necessary in itself or possible in itself. And the intuition judges that the necessary in itself does not admit non-existence. And the intuition attests that that necessary in itself is either free or necessitating. And the intuition judges that the possible in itself must terminate at the necessary in itself, either without intermediary or with one intermediary or with many intermediaries. Then the intuition attests that the effect of the necessary in itself must persist with the persistence of that cause, and since that agent is not a necessitator – and if this is invalidated, it is established that the agent is a free actor. And the intuition attests that everything that is an act of a free actor is originated. So it is established by this that everything that non-existence is valid for – the eternal must not have non-existence valid for it. And what you have mentioned of objections runs in the course of impugning necessary truths. So no attention is paid to it – and God knows best.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage presents the fifth objection against the proof for a free creator and its answer using rational intuition (badīha). The objector concedes that the agent is a necessitator (muʾaththir mūjib) but argues that its perpetuity does not necessitate the perpetuity of its effect, because the effect may depend on a privative condition. For example, gravity causes a heavy object to fall only if there is no restraining chain. Similarly, the creation of the world might have been conditioned on an eternal privative condition (e.g., the non-existence of a hindrance), and that condition could cease, so the effect (the world) would cease. The answer rejects this by appealing to self-evident judgments of reason. First, reason directly knows that existents are either necessary in themselves (wājib li-dhātihi) or possible in themselves (mumkin li-dhātihi). Second, the necessary in itself cannot admit non-existence. Third, the necessary in itself is either free (mukhtār) or necessitating (mūjib). Fourth, every possible being must terminate at the necessary being, directly or indirectly. Fifth, reason attests that the effect of the necessary being must endure as long as its cause endures. Since the world is not eternal (as shown by other arguments), the cause cannot be a mere necessitator, because then the effect would be perpetual. Therefore, the cause must be a free agent. Sixth, any act of a free agent is originated (muḥdath). Hence, whatever can admit non-existence is originated, and the eternal (the necessary being) cannot admit non-existence. The objector's arguments are thus attacks on self-evident principles and should be ignored.

Key Terms
شرط عدمي
موجب
مؤثر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Perpetuity of cause always necessitates perpetuity of effect, ignoring possible conditions.
Correction: The effect may depend on privative conditions (like absence of a hindrance), so the effect may cease even if the cause is perpetual.

Checkpoint
According to the objection, what condition might prevent the effect from being perpetual?
A) A positive condition
B) A privative condition
C) No condition
D) A temporal condition

Key Takeaway
The objection argues that a necessitating agent's effect may not be perpetual if it depends on a privative condition that could cease.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
In your own life, do you rely on certain 'privative conditions'—like the absence of temptation or the presence of a supportive environment—to maintain your faith and good deeds? What if those conditions cease? Are you prepared for that, or is your faith conditional?
?
This lesson shows that even a necessitating agent's effect can cease if a privative condition vanishes. Think of a time you felt spiritually stagnant or distant from Allah. Was it because some condition you were relying on disappeared? What does that reveal about the nature of your relationship with your Creator?
?
The objector uses an analogy of a heavy object and a chain. What 'chains' in your life are currently preventing you from falling into sin or negligence? Are you grateful for them, or do you take them for granted? How can you strengthen your connection to Allah so that even if those chains are removed, you remain steadfast?

The Answer: Rational Intuitions Establish a Free Creator
Answers the objection using a series of self-evident rational judgments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the answer uses rational intuitions (badīha) to refute the objection and establish that the Creator is a free agent whose acts are originated.

Core Idea
Reason directly knows that the cause of a possible being must be necessary and its effect must persist.

The objector's argument is rejected by appealing to self-evident judgments of reason. The answer enumerates several intuitive truths about necessary and possible beings, culminating in the conclusion that the agent is free and the world is originated. These intuitions are considered necessary truths that cannot be rationally contested.

Guided Path
1
Read the answer passage
Read the Arabic answer from 'والجواب' to the end, then its translation. Notice the repeated phrase 'والبديهة حاكمة' or 'شاهدة'.
Each occurrence introduces a self-evident judgment.
2
List the intuitive judgments
Identify each of the six judgments: (1) existents are necessary or possible, (2) necessary does not admit non-existence, (3) necessary is either free or necessitating, (4) possible beings end at a necessary being, (5) effect of necessary persists with its cause, (6) act of a free agent is originated.
These are presented in order.
3
Understand the refutation
The answer argues that since the world is not eternal (as proven elsewhere), the cause cannot be a mere necessitator; otherwise its effect would be perpetual. Therefore, the cause must be a free agent, and the world is originated.
The objection is dismissed as an attack on necessary truths.

The Moon's Eclipses Reveal Its Dependency on the Sun
The author argues that the moon's eclipses reveal its dependency on the sun.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the moon's phases and eclipses demonstrate that its light is borrowed from the sun and how eclipses serve as a key to locating celestial bodies.

Core Idea
The moon's light is accidental, not essential; eclipses unlock the positions of the stars.

This passage presents the second benefit in a series: the moon's variable light and eclipses. The author argues that the moon's light waxes and wanes due to its distance from the sun, and many believe all planets borrow their light from the sun. Without eclipses, we could not determine the moon's true position because of parallax, and without that, we could not locate other stars. Thus, eclipses are a key astronomical tool.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's argument clearly.
Notice the logical flow: from observation of moonlight to eclipses to practical utility.
2
Identify the two key claims
The passage makes two main points: (1) the moon's light is accidental, acquired from the sun, and (2) lunar eclipses are essential for determining the true positions of celestial bodies.
3
Reflect on the reasoning
Why does the author say that if the moon had essential light, it would not eclipse? And why is knowing the moon's true position necessary for other stars? Trace the causal chain.
This connects to the learning objective about dependency and utility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثاني : أن القمر يزداد نوره وينتقص ، بسبب قربه من الشمس ، وبعده عنها ، وكثيرون من الناس يزعمون : أن أنوار سائر الكواكب مقتبسة من الشمس، ولولا أن جرم القمر ليس نوره نوراً ذاتياً ، بل عرضياً مستفاداً من الشمس ، وإلا لما عرض له الخسوف . ولولا الخسوف لتعذر معرفة موضعه الحقيقي من الفلك ، بسبب ما يحصل فيه من اختلاف المنظر ، لأجل قربه من الأرض . ولو لم يعرف الموضع الحقيقي للقمر ، لتعذر معرفة المواضع الحقيقية لسائر الكواكب. فكان حصول الخسوف للقمر ، كالمفتاح المعرفة مواضع الأجرام النيرة الفلكية .
The second aspect: that the moon increases and decreases in its light due to its proximity to the sun and distance from it. Many people claim that the lights of other planets are borrowed from the sun. Were it not that the body of the moon does not have essential light but accidental light acquired from the sun, otherwise it would not be subject to eclipse. Without the eclipse, it would be impossible to know its true position in the sky because of the parallax occurring in it due to its proximity to the earth. And if the true position of the moon were not known, it would be impossible to know the true positions of the other planets. So the occurrence of the eclipse of the moon is like a key to knowing the positions of the luminous celestial bodies.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage presents the second benefit: the moon's variable light and eclipses. The author notes that the moon's light waxes and wanes depending on its distance from the sun. Many hold that the planets' light is borrowed from the sun. The moon's light is accidental, not essential; otherwise there would be no eclipses. Without eclipses, we could not determine the moon's true position due to parallax (caused by its nearness to earth). And if the moon's position is unknown, the positions of other stars become uncertain. Thus, eclipses serve as a key to locating celestial bodies.

Correction: The passage argues that the moon's light is accidental, acquired from the sun, as evidenced by eclipses and varying phases.

Checkpoint

D) They show that the moon is farther from Earth than other planets.

Key Takeaway
Lunar eclipses, by revealing the moon's borrowed light, are essential for determining the positions of stars.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Sun's Heat and Planetary Influence
The author explains how the sun's heat varies with the planets it accompanies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the sun's heat is modulated by the planets it aligns with during its course, as explained by the author.

Core Idea
The sun's heat is influenced by the planets it accompanies, even when they are hidden.

This lesson explores the third benefit discussed by the author: the variation in the sun's heat due to its conjunction with other planets. The author explains why some summer days are hotter than others, attributing it to the hidden power of planets that align with the sun. This teaches us about causality and the interconnectedness of celestial bodies.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Notice the cause-and-effect relationship the author describes between the sun and other planets.
The passage is short but dense. Read it slowly.
2
Identify the key claim
The author claims that the sun's radiance hides other planets, but their power remains. This sets up the explanation for heat variation.
3
Understand the conclusion
The conclusion is that alignment with a hot planet increases heat, and opposite for cold. This explains why some summer days are hotter.
The author uses 'conjunction' (قارنت) to describe the alignment.
4
Reflect on broader significance
Think about how this example illustrates causality and points to a divine order. The author is building an argument for the existence of a higher power.
Consider the subtopic 'causality' and 'divine existence'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثالث : أن الشمس إذا ظهرت ، اختفت بكمال شعاعها سائر الكواكب ، إلا أنها وإن خفيت ، إلا أن قوتها باقية. ولذلك فإنه يكون يوم من الصيف ، أحر من يوم آخر . وما ذاك إلا بسبب أن الشمس إذا قارنت في سيرها كوكباً حاراً ، فإنه يزداد حر الهواء ، وبالضد منه في جانب البرد .
The third aspect: that when the sun appears, all other planets disappear due to its complete radiance, but even though they are hidden, their power remains. Therefore, one summer day is hotter than another day. That is only because the sun, when it aligns in its course with a hot planet, the heat of the air increases, and the opposite applies on the side of cold.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage gives the third benefit: the sun's heat is modulated by other planets. When the sun rises, its brilliance obscures the other stars, yet they still exert influence. Hence, some summer days are hotter than others due to the sun's conjunction with a hot planet, which amplifies the air's heat. Conversely, conjunction with a cold planet causes cooler conditions.

Key Terms

حرارة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sun's heat is constant and only varies due to Earth's distance or orbit.
Correction: The author argues that the sun's heat is modulated by the hidden influence of planets it aligns with, not by distance or other factors.

Checkpoint

B) The sun aligns with a hot planet during its course.

Key Takeaway
The sun's heat varies because of its alignment with other planets, whose influence remains even when hidden.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

The Sixth Benefit: Apogee and Perigee Expose Land
The author explains the sixth benefit of the sun: its apogee and perigee expose land for habitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the causal mechanism by which the sun's apogee and perigee expose land for habitation, and how this reveals divine design.

Core Idea
The sun's orbital motion creates habitable land by drawing vapors away.

In this passage, the author presents the sixth benefit of the sun's existence: the exposure of land through its apogee and perigee. He builds a causal chain from the sun's motion to the drawing of vapors, resulting in dry land suitable for animals and humans. This argument exemplifies the teleological reasoning common in Islamic theology, pointing to purpose in creation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the causal language: فعند, فتعظم, فلا جرم indicating results.
The author uses a step-by-step reasoning.
2
Trace the causal chain
Identify each step: sun's orbit → apogee/perigee → far/near → heat intensifies near perigee → heat attracts vapors → vapors drawn to perigee side → opposite side exposed → land emerges.
This shows how each effect follows from the previous cause.
3
Reflect on the purpose
The author presents this as a benefit (منفعة). Consider why this is seen as a sign of divine wisdom.
The ultimate beneficiary is man, as the noblest animal.
4
Address the misconception
Contrast with the common idea that apogee/perigee only cause seasons. The author stresses land exposure for habitation.
This illustrates the teleological perspective in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه السادس من منافع وجود الشمس : إنه تعالى حركها . بحيث يحصل لها في الحركة أوج وحضيض ، فعند حصولها في الأوج تبعد عن الأرض ، وعند حصولها في الحضيض تقرب من الأرض . وبسبب القرب من الأرض ، تعظم السخونة من المواضع التي يحاذيها مدار الحضيض ، والسخونة جاذبة للرطوبات ، فلا جرم تجذب البخار إلى الجانب الذي يسامته حضيض الشمس ، وإذا انجذب البخار إلى ذلك الجانب ، انكشف الجانب الذي يحاذيه الأوج ، ولم يبق البحر على وجهه ، فصار أحد جوانب الأرض ، صالحاً لمساكن الحيوانات البرية . لا سيما الإنسان الذي هو أشرف الحيوانات الموجودة في عالم الكون والفساد .
The sixth aspect of the benefits of the existence of the sun: He, exalted, moved it such that it acquires in its motion an apogee and a perigee. When it is at apogee, it is far from the earth, and when it is at perigee, it is near the earth. Due to its proximity to the earth, the heat intensifies in the places that are opposite the orbit of perigee, and heat attracts vapors. So inevitably it draws vapor to the side that is in line with the perigee of the sun. When the vapor is drawn to that side, the side that is opposite the apogee becomes exposed, and the sea is no longer on its surface. Thus one side of the earth becomes suitable for the habitation of land animals, especially man, who is the noblest of animals existing in the world of generation and corruption.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage presents the sixth benefit of the sun: the creation of an apogee and perigee in the sun's orbit. The author explains that when the sun is at perigee (closer to Earth), heat increases, attracting vapors (moisture) to that side. This draws vapor away from the opposite side (the apogee side), causing the sea to recede and exposing land. This exposed land becomes suitable for land animals, especially humans. The argument is causal and teleological, showing divine wisdom in the design of the sun's motion to create habitable land.

Key Terms

حضيض
السخونة
الرطوبات
البخار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sun's apogee and perigee only affect seasonal temperatures.
Correction: The author argues they also cause land exposure through vapor attraction, making land habitable.

Checkpoint
According to the sixth benefit, what directly happens when the sun is at perigee?
A) The land becomes colder.
B) Vapors are attracted to that side.
C) The sea rises.
D) The earth becomes flat.

Key Takeaway
The sun's apogee and perigee are divinely designed to expose land through a causal chain of heat and vapor attraction, making Earth habitable.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see the sun rise and set each day, do you pause to consider that its entire orbital motion is precisely calibrated to make this planet your home? How can you train yourself to see the sun as a sign of Allah's care rather than a mere celestial clock?
?
The author states that man is the noblest of animals in this world. Do you live with that dignity, or do you allow your desires and distractions to pull you away from your purpose? What 'vapor' in your life needs to be drawn away so that the land of your heart can be exposed for worship?
?
If the sun's apogee and perigee are not random but divinely designed for your benefit, what does that imply about how you should respond to the other 'mundane' natural events in your life? Will you now look for the hand of Allah behind every cause and effect?

The Seventh Benefit: Extreme Cold at the Poles
Description of polar conditions and empirical evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the sun's distance from perpendicular causes extreme cold at the poles, making them uninhabitable, and recognize the empirical evidence from the Armenian and Syrian Seas.

Core Idea
The poles' extreme cold is a sign of the sun's perfect placement.

The author continues to enumerate the benefits of the sun by examining what happens when the sun is far from perpendicular: intense cold. He describes the harsh conditions at the poles, then supports his claim with observations from two seas that become unnavigable due to cold and storms.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its English translation. Notice the structure: first a general principle, then description of the poles, then two pieces of evidence.
2
Identify the conditions at the poles
List the phenomena mentioned: no animals, no plants, six months of day/night, violent winds, intense darkness. These illustrate the severity of cold.
The author uses these to emphasize the extreme nature of the poles.
3
Examine the evidence from the seas
Look at the Armenian Sea and the Syrian Sea examples. The Armenian Sea, though closer to the sun's orbit, is still so cold and dark it cannot be sailed. The Syrian Sea is unnavigable in winter months.
This shows that even moderately far locations suffer, so the poles must be much worse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه السابع من منافع الشمس : إن كان موضع تكون الشمس بعيد جداً عن مسامتها ، اشتد البرد فيه . مثل الموضعين اللذين تحت القطبين ، فإنه لا يتكون هناك حيوان ، ولا ينبت فيه نبات ويكون هناك ستة أشهر نهاراً . وستة أخرى ليلا . ويكون هناك رياح عاصفة، وتشتد ظلمته . ويدل عليه أنه البحر الأرمني ، فإنه أقرب إلى مدار الشمس من الموضع المذكور بكثير، مع تشتد فيه الرياح العواصف ، وتشتد ظلمته ، حتى لا يمكن ركوبه لشدة برده وظلمته . ويستدل عليه أيضاً بالبحر الشامي، فإنه إذا صارت الشمس في أوائل العقرب ، إلى أن تصير إلى أوائل الحوت : ففي هذه الأشهر لا يستطيع الناس ركوبه
The seventh aspect of the benefits of the sun: If the place where the sun is formed is very far from its perpendicular, the cold becomes intense in it. Like the two places under the poles: no animal is formed there, no plant grows, and there is six months of day and six months of night. There are violent winds and intense darkness. Evidence for this is the Armenian Sea, for it is much closer to the orbit of the sun than the aforementioned place, yet the winds become violent and its darkness intense, so much so that it cannot be sailed due to its severe cold and darkness. Evidence is also drawn from the Syrian Sea: when the sun is in the beginning of Scorpio until it reaches the beginning of Pisces, during these months people cannot sail it.
Source pages p. 335

Commentary
This passage presents the seventh benefit: the sun's distance from perpendicular causes extreme cold at the poles, making them uninhabitable—no animals, no plants, six months of day and night, violent winds, and darkness. The author then gives empirical evidence: the Armenian Sea, though closer to the sun's orbit than the poles, still experiences violent winds and darkness making it unnavigable due to cold. Similarly, the Syrian Sea becomes unnavigable during the months when the sun is in Scorpio and Pisces (winter months). This demonstrates how extreme the conditions would be if the sun were even farther, thus showing the wisdom in its current distance.

The Sun as Cause of Human Diversity: An Inductive Argument
Author uses induction to link sun's motion to human diversity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author uses induction to argue that the sun's motion is the apparent cause of differences in human bodies, colors, and morals, and how he classifies humanity into three climatic zones.

Core Idea
Sunlight shapes humanity: from equator to pole, climate writes our story.

The author presents the eighth benefit of studying celestial motions: explaining human diversity. He uses induction (استقراء) to argue that the sun's varying position directly affects people's physical and moral characteristics. This lesson explores his tripartite classification of humanity based on proximity to the equator and the sun's perpendicular rays.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the literal translation. Let the author’s argument come through before you interpret.
Pay attention to the terms for the three groups: السودان, البيضان, and the subgroups.
2
Identify the three human groups
The author divides people into three types based on their location relative to the equator and the sun's path. List each group and its characteristics (body, color, morals).
Notice the progression from equatorial to northern regions.
3
Understand the causal mechanism
The author claims the sun’s heat causes the differences. Ask yourself: How does the sun’s position affect each group? Why is this considered a divine wisdom?
This connects to the learning objective and the inductive method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوجه الثامن : أن الاستقراء يدل على أن السبب الظاهر لاختلاف الناس في أجسامهم وألوانهم وأخلاقهم وطبائعهم وسيرهم : اختلاف أحوال الشمس في الحركة. وذلك لأن الناس على ثلاثة أقسام . أحدها : الذين يسكنون خط الإستواء إلى ما يقرب من المواضع التي يحاذيها ممر رأس السرطان ، وهم يسمون بالاسم العام السودان ، والسبب فيه أن الشمس تنزل على سمت رؤوسهم في السنة. إما مرة أو مرتين ، فتحرقهم وتسود أبدانهم وشعورهم. والذين مساكنهم أقرب إلى خط الإستواء فهم الزنج ، والحبشة ، فإن الشمس لقوة تأثيرها في مساكنهم تحرق شعورهم وتسودها ، وتجعلها جعدة وكثيفة فحلة ، وجثثهم عظيمة ، وأخلاقهم وحشية ، وأما الذين مساكنهم أقرب إلى محاذاة ممر رأس السرطان ، فالسواد فيهم أقل ، أعدل ، وأخلاقهم الين ، وأجسامهم أضعف . وهم أهل الهند واليمن، وبعض المغاربة ، وكل العرب وطبائعهم وأما القسم الثاني من أهل الأرض : فهم الذين مساكنهم على ممر رأس السرطان ، إلى محاذاة بنات نعش الكبرى ، وهم يسمون بالاسم العام البيضان، وهؤلاء لأجل أن الشمس لا تسامت رؤوسهم، ولا تبعد أيضاً عنهم بعداً
The eighth aspect: Induction indicates that the apparent cause of the differences among people in their bodies, colors, morals, natures, and behaviors is the difference in the states of the sun in its motion. People are of three types. The first: those who inhabit the equator to near the places opposite the path of the Tropic of Cancer; they are called by the general name 'Sudan' (blacks). The reason is that the sun passes directly overhead once or twice a year, burning them and blackening their bodies and hair. Those whose dwellings are closer to the equator are the Zanj and the Habasha (Ethiopians); the sun, due to the strength of its effect on their dwellings, burns their hair and blackens it, making it curly, thick, and kinky, and their bodies are large and their morals wild. As for those whose dwellings are closer to the opposite of the path of the Tropic of Cancer, the blackness is less and more moderate, their morals are softer, and their bodies weaker. They are the people of India, Yemen, some Maghrebis, and all the Arabs. The second type of earth's inhabitants: those whose dwellings are on the path of the Tropic of Cancer up to the opposite of the Big Dipper (Ursa Major); they are called by the general name 'Bidan' (whites). These, because the sun is not directly overhead nor too far from them...
Source pages p. 336

Commentary
This passage presents the eighth benefit: the sun's motion causes diversity in human physical and moral characteristics. The author uses induction (استقراء) to argue that the apparent cause is the difference in the sun's position. He divides humanity into three groups based on their distance from the equator: (1) Equatorial and near-equatorial peoples (Sudan, Zanj, Habasha) who are black, have curly hair, large bodies, and wild morals due to the sun burning them directly. (2) Those closer to the Tropic of Cancer (people of India, Yemen, some Maghrebis, and all Arabs) who have less blackness, more moderate morals, and weaker bodies. (3) Those from the Tropic of Cancer to near Ursa Major (called 'Bidan', whites) who are not directly exposed nor too far from the sun. The passage is an early attempt at geographic determinism, attributing human diversity to climate and sun exposure, demonstrating divine wisdom in creating variety.

البيضان
الزنج
الحبشة
رأس السرطان
بنات نعش الكبرى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author is making a racist claim about black and white people.
Correction: The author uses observed geographical variations to argue for a natural cause (the sun) as part of divine wisdom, not promoting racial hierarchy.

First Objection: Lack of Medicines
Al-Razi presents the first objection and answers it using the principle of moderation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the absence of medicines in the fourth climate does not refute its superiority, and how Al-Razi uses the concept of moderation to explain it.

Core Idea
Medicines require imbalance; the fourth climate's balance explains their absence.

In defending the fourth climate's superiority, Al-Razi anticipates an objection: if it is the best, why are medicinal herbs not found there? This objection seems to suggest a deficiency. Al-Razi's answer introduces a key principle: medicines are by nature imbalanced, and the fourth climate's perfect moderation naturally produces only balanced foods. Let's read his precise argument.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how the objection is stated as a challenge to the claim of superiority.
The objection uses the phrase 'لا يتولد شيء منها' to emphasize total absence.
2
Identify key concepts
Look for the terms 'اعتدال' (moderation) and 'غلبة' (dominance). Understand that medicines require a dominant quality and dominant solar power.
3
Understand the causal reasoning
Al-Razi argues that the fourth climate's moderation prevents the production of imbalances needed for medicines. This turns the objection into a confirmation of its superiority.
Contrast the fourth climate with 'الأقاليم الخارجة عن الاعتدال' (climates outside moderation).
4
Reflect on the theological point
Consider how this explanation preserves the idea that the fourth climate is best despite lacking medicines. It aligns with divine wisdom in creating diverse climates.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل: زعمتم: أن الإقليم الرابع أفضل الأقاليم. وعليه سؤالان: الأول: أن الأدوية النافعة لا يتولد شيء منها في الإقليم الرابع، وإنما يتولد في سائر الأقاليم. والثاني: إنه لم يخرج من هذا الإقليم أحد من الأنبياء [والرسل]. والجواب عن الأول: إن الدواء إنما يكون دواء، إذا كانت إحدى الكيفيات غالبة، وكانت القوة الشمسية غالبة عليه. وهذا إنما يتولد في الأقاليم الخارجة عن الاعتدال. أما الإقليم الرابع، فإنه لما كان معتدلاً، لا جرم لا يتولد فيه إلا الأجسام الغذائية المعتدلة. أما الأجسام الدوائية، فإنها لا بد وأن تكون خارجة عن الاعتدال. فلهذا السبب لا تتولد الأدوية في هذا الإقليم. والجواب عن السؤال الثاني: إن عقول أهل الإقليم الرابع كاملة، غزيرتهم متوافرة، وبعضهم يقرب من البعض في الكمال، فلا جرم لم يخرج الأنبياء. أما سائر الأقاليم فالنقصان غالب عليهم، فإذا اتفق خروج إنسان كامل عظيم الكمال، لاجرم ظهر التفاوت، منتهيا إلى حد الإعجاز منهم. والله أعلم.
If it is said: You claim that the fourth climate is the best of the climates. There are two objections upon it: First, that beneficial medicines are not produced at all in the fourth climate, but are produced in the other climates. Second, that none of the prophets [and messengers] came out from this climate. The answer to the first: Medicine is only medicine when one of the qualities is dominant and the solar power is dominant over it. This is only produced in the climates outside moderation. As for the fourth climate, since it is moderate, inevitably only balanced nutritional bodies are produced in it. As for medicinal bodies, they must necessarily be outside moderation. For this reason medicines are not produced in this climate. The answer to the second question: The minds of the inhabitants of the fourth climate are perfect, their natural disposition (gharizatuhum) is abundant, and some are close to others in perfection, so inevitably the prophets did not come out. As for the other climates, deficiency dominates them, so if a perfect human of great perfection happens to come out, inevitably the difference appears reaching the level of miracle (i'jaz) from them. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument defending the superiority of the fourth climate by addressing two objections. The author first presents the objections: (1) beneficial medicines are not produced in the fourth climate but elsewhere, (2) no prophets came from the fourth climate. Then he answers each. The first answer explains that medicines require an imbalance of qualities and dominance of solar force, which occurs in non-moderate climates. The fourth climate is moderate, so it produces only balanced foods, not medicines. The second answer argues that the minds of the fourth climate inhabitants are perfect and nearly equal, so no single individual stands out enough to be a prophet. In other climates, deficiency dominates, so an exceptionally perfect person appears as a miracle. The passage concludes with 'And God knows best.'

Key Terms
الإقليم الرابع
الأدوية
الاعتدال
القوة الشمسية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The absence of medicines in the fourth climate proves it is inferior or less useful.
Correction: Medicines require imbalance; the fourth climate's perfect moderation naturally excludes them, so their absence actually highlights its superiority.

Checkpoint

A) Because the climate is too cold.
B) Because medicines require imbalance and solar dominance.
C) Because the inhabitants do not need them.
D) Because the sun is not strong enough.

Key Takeaway
The fourth climate's moderation explains why it produces no medicines; this reinforces its superiority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

How can you shift your focus from seeking remedies to building a nourished soul?
?
Al-Razi argues that the absence of medicines is actually a proof of perfection. What is one area of your life where you have been complaining about what is missing, but upon reflection, that 'absence' might actually be a sign of Allah's wisdom and mercy for you? Second Objection: No Prophets from the Fourth Climate
Al-Razi presents the second objection and answers it by appealing to the intellectual perfection of the fourth climate's inhabitants.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the absence of prophets from the fourth climate is explained by the perfect and equal intellectual abilities of its inhabitants.

Core Idea
Perfect minds in the fourth climate need no prophets; miracles appear in less perfect climates.

A second objection challenges the fourth climate's superiority: none of the prophets came from there. How can a region be best without producing the best of humanity? Al-Razi's answer turns to the intellectual perfection of its inhabitants—their near equality in ability means no single individual stands out as a miraculous prophet. In other climates, the general deficiency makes a perfect person's rise a clear miracle. Let's read his reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the second objection and answer
Read the Arabic and translation. Note that the objection mentions both prophets and messengers, and the answer focuses on intellectual perfection.
2
Analyze the explanation for no prophets
Al-Razi says the minds of the fourth climate's inhabitants are perfect and abundant, and they are close to each other in perfection. Thus no one is distinguished enough to be a prophet.
Key phrase: 'وبعضهم يقرب من البعض في الكمال'
3
Understand the contrast with other climates
In other climates, deficiency predominates, so an exceptionally perfect person appears as a miracle (إعجاز). This explains why prophets come from those regions.
4
Reflect on the theological implication
Prophethood is a divine gift that stands out against a backdrop of imperfection. The fourth climate's near-perfection obviates the need for such a stark distinction.
This aligns with the idea that the fourth climate is best in a different sense.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If it is said: You claim that the fourth climate is the best of the climates. There are two objections upon it: First, that beneficial medicines are not produced at all in the fourth climate, but are produced in the other climates. Second, that none of the prophets [and messengers] came out from this climate. The answer to the first: Medicine is only medicine when one of the qualities is dominant and the solar power is dominant over it. This is only produced in the climates outside moderation. As for the fourth climate, since it is moderate, inevitably only balanced nutritional bodies are produced in it. As for medicinal bodies, they must necessarily be outside moderation. For this reason medicines are not produced in this climate. The answer to the second question: The minds of the inhabitants of the fourth climate are perfect, their natural disposition (gharizatuhum) is abundant, and some are close to others in perfection, so inevitably the prophets did not come out. As for the other climates, deficiency dominates them, so if a perfect human of great perfection happens to come out, inevitably the difference appears reaching the level of miracle (i'jaz) from them. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 338

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument defending the superiority of the fourth climate by addressing two objections. The author first presents the objections: (1) beneficial medicines are not produced in the fourth climate but elsewhere, (2) no prophets came from the fourth climate. Then he answers each. The first answer explains that medicines require an imbalance of qualities and dominance of solar force, which occurs in non-moderate climates. The fourth climate is moderate, so it produces only balanced foods, not medicines. The second answer argues that the minds of the fourth climate inhabitants are perfect and nearly equal, so no single individual stands out enough to be a prophet. In other climates, deficiency dominates, so an exceptionally perfect person appears as a miracle. The passage concludes with 'And God knows best.'

Key Terms
الأنبياء
الكمال
الإعجاز
النقصان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The absence of prophets from the fourth climate proves it is inferior or less favored by God.
Correction: The fourth climate's inhabitants are so uniformly perfect that no single person is distinguished; prophethood arises in climates where a perfect individual stands out against general deficiency.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Razi, what is the reason no prophets came from the fourth climate?
A) The inhabitants were too sinful.
B) The inhabitants were all equally perfect, so no one stood out.
C) The climate was too hot for revelation.
D) God chose only from other climates arbitrarily.

Key Takeaway
The fourth climate's lack of prophets is due to its inhabitants' near-universal perfection, not inferiority.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you content with your intellectual abilities, or do you recognize your need for divine guidance? How does al-Razi's assertion about the fourth climate's perfection challenge your view of human sufficiency?
?
When you see people of great intellect who reject prophecy, do you assume they are arrogant? Or could they, like the fourth climate's inhabitants, be blinded by their own perfection?
?
Al-Razi says miracles appear where deficiency is overcome. Do you seek the miraculous in your own life, or do you rely on your natural abilities to the point of ignoring divine signs?

The Sun's Role in Seasons and Plant Growth
Two aspects: seasons as cause of plant life, and detailed mechanism of plant growth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the sun's movement causes the four seasons and how this leads to plant growth, establishing the sun as the ultimate natural cause of worldly events.

Core Idea
The sun is the ultimate cause of all events through the seasons and plant growth.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah presents two aspects of the sun's effects: first on the seasons, then on plant growth. The author traces a causal chain from the sun's movement to the seasons, then to plants, and ultimately to animals, showing the sun as the primary cause. Read carefully to see the detailed mechanism of how the sun's position affects the earth's interior and leads to plant development.

Guided Path
1
Read and identify the two aspects
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice that it begins with 'الوجه العاشر' (the tenth aspect) and 'الوجه الحادي عشر' (the eleventh aspect). These are two distinct but connected discussions.
The tenth aspect focuses on seasons; the eleventh on plant growth mechanism.
2
Trace the causal chain
Identify the chain: sun movement → four seasons → plant generation/ripening/perfection → animal generation → all worldly events. The author calls the sun the 'origin' (الأصل) for all events.
Note the logical connectives: 'فلما كان السبب...' (Since the cause...).
3
Analyze the plant growth mechanism
Focus on the eleventh aspect. Note the two phases: when sun is far from zenith (cold surface, heat inside earth, fine vapors, seed splitting) and when sun returns (cold departs, moderate air, fragments emerge, ripening).
The passage uses 'ثم' (then) to sequence the process.
4
Reflect on the overall claim
Consider why the author emphasizes that the sun is 'like the origin for all events.' This elevates the sun to a primary natural cause, though indirect.
This connects to broader themes of causality in Islamic thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه العاشر من تأثيرات الشمس : اختلاف الفصول الأربعة ، بسبب انتقالها في ارباع الفلك . ولا شك : أن السبب في تولد النباتات ونضجها وكمال حالها ، ليس إلا هذه الفصول الأربعة . فلما كان السبب لحدوث الفصول الأربعة هو الشمس والسبب لتولد الحيوانات هو النبات ، صارت الشمس كالأصل لكل حوادث هذا العالم . الوجه الحادي عشر في تأثير الشمس في النبات : وهو من وجوه : أحدهما : إن الشمس إذا تباعدت عن سمت الرأس ، اشتد البرد في الهواء ، واستولى البرد على ظاهر الأرض . فيقوى الحر في باطن الأرض ، ويتولد فيه الأبخرة اللطيفة ، الموافقة لتكون المعادن ، وانفلاق الحب في بطن الأرض . فإذا مالت الشمس إلى سمت الرؤوس، وزال البرد ، واعتدل الهواء ، خرجت تلك الشظايا من بطن الأرض إلى ظهرها . ثم إن الهواء المسخن بسبب قوة الشمس ، تؤثر فيه الشمس . فيحصل النضج والكمال في الزروع والثمار .
The tenth aspect of the sun's effects: the variation of the four seasons, due to its movement in the quadrants of the celestial sphere. There is no doubt that the cause of the generation, ripening, and perfection of plants is nothing but these four seasons. Since the cause of the occurrence of the four seasons is the sun, and the cause of the generation of animals is plants, the sun became like the origin for all events of this world. The eleventh aspect concerning the sun's effect on plants: and it is from among aspects: one of them: when the sun moves away from the zenith, the cold intensifies in the air and overwhelms the surface of the earth. Then heat strengthens in the interior of the earth, and there generate fine vapors suitable for the formation of minerals and the splitting of seeds in the belly of the earth. Then when the sun inclines toward the zeniths, the cold departs, the air becomes moderate, those fragments come out from the belly of the earth to its surface. Then the air heated by the sun's power acts upon them, and the sun affects them. So ripening and perfection occur in crops and fruits.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage presents two aspects (wajhan) of the sun's effects. The tenth aspect explains that the four seasons are caused by the sun's movement through the quadrants of the celestial sphere. These seasons are the sole cause of the generation, ripening, and perfection of plants. Since animals depend on plants, the sun becomes the original cause of all events in this world. The eleventh aspect details the mechanism of plant growth: when the sun is far from the zenith, cold dominates the surface, but heat strengthens inside the earth, generating fine vapors that help form minerals and split seeds. When the sun returns toward the zenith, cold leaves, the air becomes moderate, and the fragments emerge from the earth. Then the heated air and the sun's power cause ripening and perfection in crops and fruits.

Key Terms
فصول
سمت الرأس
أبخرة لطيفة
انفلاق الحب
نضج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sun directly causes plant growth by shining on them.
Correction: The passage shows a multi-step process: the sun's position causes seasons, which create underground heat and vapors that split seeds; only after the sun returns does the heated air cause ripening.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens when the sun is far from the zenith?
A) The interior of the earth becomes colder.
B) Heat strengthens in the interior of the earth.
C) Plants immediately grow.
D) The air becomes very hot.

Key Takeaway
The sun's movement through the celestial quadrants causes the four seasons, which directly cause plant generation and perfection, making the sun the ultimate natural cause of all worldly events.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you see the seasons change and plants grow, do you pause to recognize that these are not random events but part of a divinely appointed causal order? Are you grateful to the Almighty who set this system in motion, or do you take it for granted?
?
If the sun's movement is merely a means (sabab) and not an independent cause, does your reliance on natural processes ever distract you from placing your ultimate trust in Allah? Today, consciously attribute the ripening of a fruit or the warmth of the sun to His will.
?
The passage describes how underground vapors and heat prepare seeds to split and emerge at the right time. Consider a difficulty in your life that has been 'underground' — a trial or a period of waiting. Do you believe that Allah is working through hidden means to bring about good in its proper season? What would it look like for you to trust His timing?

The Sun's Influence on Human Diversity
Author explains how the sun causes differences in human forms, colors, and morals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author attributes both physical and moral differences among humans to the sun's varying effects, mediated by climate and temperament.

Core Idea
The sun shapes not only our bodies but also our characters.

This passage from Al-Matalibul Aliyah explains how the sun is the primary cause of human diversity. The author describes how the sun's proximity and distance influence physical traits, and how moral differences stem from temperaments shaped by climate. Through examples, we see a deterministic but designed causal order.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the description of the people of the sixth and seventh clime.
The passage has a logical flow from specific to general.
2
Identify the two causes
Distinguish between the cause of physical differences (sun's proximity/distance) and moral differences (temperaments).
Moral differences are secondary, dependent on temperaments.
3
Analyze the examples
Consider the examples of Indians (strong imagination), Turks (courage), and Maghribis (bad character). How do they illustrate the principle?
These examples show that specific traits are linked to specific climates.
4
Reflect on causality
Think about the causal chain: sun → climate → temperament → morality. Why does the author emphasize the sun's role?
This reflects a teleological understanding of divine design.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أهل الإقليم السادس والسابع فأهلهم سود، ولغلبة البرد والرطوبة عليهم، اشتد بياض ألوانهم، وزرق عيونهم، وعظمت وجوههم، واستدارت. فقد تبين: أن اختلاف طبائع الناس في صورهم وأشكالهم وألوانهم، بسبب اختلاف أحوال الشمس في القرب والبعد. وأما اختلاف الناس في الأخلاق والطبائع، فهو تابع لاختلاف أمزجتهم. فإن الوهم المؤثر الذي للهند، لا يكاد يوجد في غيرهم. وكذلك الشجاعة في الترك، وسوء الخلق في المغاربة، لا يوجد مثله للمشارقة.
The people of the sixth and seventh clime, their people are black, and due to the prevalence of cold and humidity upon them, the whiteness of their colors intensified, and the blue of their eyes, and their faces became large and round. Thus it became clear: that the difference in the natures of people in their forms, shapes, and colors is due to the difference of the conditions of the sun in proximity and distance. As for the difference of people in morals and natures, it is dependent on the difference of their temperaments. For the effective imagination (wahm) that the Indians have is hardly found in others. Likewise, courage among the Turks, and bad character among the Maghribis, the like of it is not found among the Easterners.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage concludes that differences in human physical appearance and moral character are caused by the sun. It begins by describing the people of the sixth and seventh climes: they are black, but due to cold and humidity their whiteness intensifies (a textual oddity, likely referring to a lighter shade). The author then states that the diversity in human forms and colors results from the sun's varying proximity and distance. Moral and temperamental differences, however, are dependent on their physical temperaments (amzijah). Examples: Indians have a strong imaginative faculty, Turks are courageous, Maghribis have bad character—each trait is absent in other groups. This shows a designed causal order where the sun influences even psychological traits indirectly through climate.

Key Terms
الإقليم
الطبائع
الأخلاق
الوهم المؤثر
المزاج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Moral differences are purely arbitrary or independent of physical factors.
Correction: The author argues that moral differences are dependent on physical temperaments, which are shaped by climate influenced by the sun.

Checkpoint

A) Difference in temperaments
B) Difference in the conditions of the sun in proximity and distance
C) Difference in the phases of the moon
D) Difference in geographical latitude only

Key Takeaway
The sun is the primary cause of both physical and moral diversity among humans, acting through climate and temperament.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

How can you practically embrace someone who is different from you, recognizing that their temperament might be shaped by factors beyond their control?

The Sun as the Origin of Seasons and Life
Author demonstrates the sun as ultimate cause through a causal chain.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author argues that the sun is the ultimate cause of all events in this world through a chain of causality.

Core Idea
The sun is the root cause of everything in this world.

In this passage, the author presents a clear causal argument: the sun's movement creates the four seasons, which in turn cause plants to grow and animals to live. By tracing each effect back to its cause, he shows that the sun is the ultimate origin of all worldly events. Let's break down this logical chain step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to get the author's flow.
Notice the phrase 'كالأصل' – 'like the origin' – which is key.
2
Identify the causal links
List the chain: sun → four seasons → plants (generation, ripening, perfection) → animals. Each link is presented as a cause.
The author states 'لا شك' (no doubt) about the seasons causing plants.
3
Understand the conclusion
The author concludes: because the sun is the cause of seasons, and seasons cause plants, and plants cause animals, the sun becomes the origin of all events.
The phrase 'صارت الشمس كالأصل لكل حوادث هذا العالم' summarizes the argument.
4
Reflect on the purpose
Ask yourself: why does the author build this chain? It shows design and order in the universe, leading to the recognition of a purposeful cause.
This passage is part of a larger work on theism, pointing to a Creator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه العاشر من تأثيرات الشمس: اختلاف الفصول الأربعة، بسبب انتقالها في ارباع الفلك. ولا شك: أن السبب في تولد النباتات ونضجها وكمال حالها، ليس إلا هذه الفصول الأربعة. فلما كان السبب لحدوث الفصول الأربعة هو الشمس، والسبب لتولد الحيوانات هو النبات، صارت الشمس كالأصل لكل حوادث هذا العالم.
The tenth aspect of the effects of the sun: the difference of the four seasons, due to its movement in the quadrants of the celestial sphere. And there is no doubt that the cause of the generation of plants, their ripening, and their attainment of perfection is nothing but these four seasons. So since the cause for the occurrence of the four seasons is the sun, and the cause for the generation of animals is plants, the sun became like the origin for all events of this world.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage presents the tenth aspect of the sun's effects. The author states that the four seasons are caused by the sun's movement through the quadrants of the celestial sphere. He then asserts that the generation, ripening, and perfection of plants are entirely due to the seasons. Extending the causal chain: the sun causes seasons, seasons cause plants, and plants cause animals. Thus the sun is the ultimate origin (al-asl) of all events in this world. This establishes a clear causal hierarchy pointing to a designed order.

The Seasonal Mechanism of the Sun's Effect on Plants
Author explains the seasonal mechanism of plant growth through sun's zenith movement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the sun's seasonal movement away from and toward the zenith drives the formation of vapors in the earth, which causes seeds to split and plants to ripen.

Core Idea
Winter heat in the earth's interior prepares plants for spring growth.

This passage begins the eleventh aspect of the sun's effects on plants. It describes a seasonal process: when the sun is far from the zenith, the cold surface forces heat into the earth, generating subtle vapors that help seeds split. When the sun returns, these fragments emerge and ripen. This explanation ties together seasonal temperature changes and plant development.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the seasonal mechanism
Read the Arabic passage closely. Notice the sequence of events: sun far from zenith, cold surface, heat in earth interior, vapor generation, sun returns, emergence, ripening.
The author uses a cause-and-effect chain.
2
Identify the role of cold and heat
Observe how the cold surface forces heat into the earth's interior, creating a temperature contrast that drives vapor formation.
This is key to understanding the seasonal cycle.
3
Connect to plant growth
Reflect on how this explains the natural process from seed splitting to fruit ripening, and why it is considered a rational explanation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الحادي عشر في تأثير الشمس في النبات: وهو من وجوه: أحدهما: إن الشمس إذا تباعدت عن سمت الرأس، اشتد البرد في الهواء، واستولى البرد على ظاهر الأرض. فيقوى الحر في باطن الأرض، ويتولد فيه الأبخرة اللطيفة، الموافقة لتكون المعادن، وانفلاق الحب في بطن الأرض. فإذا مالت الشمس إلى سمت الرؤوس، وزال البرد، واعتدل الهواء، خرجت تلك الشظايا من بطن الأرض إلى ظهرها. ثم إن الهواء المسخن بسبب قوة الشمس، الشمس تؤثر فيه. فيحصل النضج والكمال في الزروع والثمار. وثانيها: إن تأثير الشمس في النبات، بسبب الحركة اليومية محسوس. والدليل عليه: أن الريحان الذي يقال له: النيلوفر، والأذيرون، وورق الخروع، وغيرها فإنها تنمو، وتزداد عند أخذ الشمس في الارتفاع والصعود. فإذا غابت الشمس ضعفت وذبلت.
The eleventh aspect concerning the effect of the sun on plants: and it is in several ways: First: When the sun moves away from the zenith, the cold intensifies in the air, and cold dominates the surface of the earth. Then heat intensifies in the interior of the earth, and there are generated in it the subtle vapors suitable for the formation of minerals, and the splitting of the seed in the belly of the earth. Then when the sun inclines toward the zenith, and the cold disappears, and the air becomes moderate, those fragments come out from the belly of the earth to its surface. Then the air heated by the strength of the sun, the sun affects it. Then ripening and perfection occur in the crops and fruits. Second: The effect of the sun on plants is perceptible due to the daily motion. The evidence for that: that the basil called the water lily (al-nilufar), and al-adhirun, and the castor bean leaves, and others—they grow and increase when the sun rises and ascends. When the sun sets, they weaken and wither.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage presents the eleventh aspect of the sun's effects on plants, enumerating multiple ways. The first way describes the seasonal mechanism: when the sun is far from the zenith (winter), cold dominates the surface, but heat concentrates in the earth's interior, generating subtle vapors that help form minerals and cause seeds to split. When the sun returns toward the zenith (spring/summer), the fragments emerge, and the heated air brings about ripening of crops and fruits. The second way is the daily effect: the author observes that certain plants like the water lily (nilufar), adhirun (perhaps a type of basil), and castor bean visibly respond to the sun's daily motion—they grow during the day and wither at night. This provides tangible evidence of the sun's direct influence on plant growth.

Key Terms
سمت الرأس
الأبخرة اللطيفة
انفلاق الحب
النضج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens when the sun moves away from the zenith?
A) Heat intensifies on the surface
B) Cold intensifies on the surface and heat in the earth's interior
C) Plants ripen immediately
D) The air becomes moderate

Key Takeaway
The sun's seasonal movement indirectly affects plant growth by altering the earth's internal temperature and vapor generation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly appreciate the intricate seasonal system Allah designed for plants, or do you take it for granted? How often do you reflect on the hidden processes that happen in winter—the heat in the earth's interior, the vapors, the seeds splitting—that make spring growth possible?
?
When you see plants growing in spring, do you remember that their life began underground during the cold months? This mechanism shows that what seems dead or dormant is actually preparing for life. Is there an area in your own life where you feel dormant or cold, but could be being prepared for a future harvest? What step will you take today to trust that process?
?
If you reflect on this passage, it reveals a wisdom that no human could have designed. Does this strengthen your belief in Allah's wisdom? What will you do differently to keep this mechanism in mind—perhaps when you see a seed or a plant—to remind yourself of the Creator behind it?

The Daily Effect of the Sun on Plants
Author provides observable evidence for the sun's daily influence on plant growth.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the sun's daily motion directly affects certain plants, as evidenced by their growth at sunrise and withering at sunset.

Core Idea
Plants like the water lily visibly respond to the sun's daily cycle.

After discussing the seasonal mechanism, the author presents a second way: the daily effect. He offers a concrete example: plants such as the water lily, adhirun, and castor bean that visibly grow during the day and wilt at night. This direct observation provides clear evidence of the sun's immediate influence on plant life.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the daily effect

The author uses observable examples to prove the daily influence.
2
Identify the specific plants mentioned

These are likely familiar to the original audience.
3

This is an empirical proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه الحادي عشر في تأثير الشمس في النبات: وهو من وجوه: أحدهما: إن الشمس إذا تباعدت عن سمت الرأس، اشتد البرد في الهواء، واستولى البرد على ظاهر الأرض. فيقوى الحر في باطن الأرض، ويتولد فيه الأبخرة اللطيفة، الموافقة لتكون المعادن، وانفلاق الحب في بطن الأرض. فإذا مالت الشمس إلى سمت الرؤوس، وزال البرد، واعتدل الهواء، خرجت تلك الشظايا من بطن الأرض إلى ظهرها. ثم إن الهواء المسخن بسبب قوة الشمس، الشمس تؤثر فيه. فيحصل النضج والكمال في الزروع والثمار. وثانيها: إن تأثير الشمس في النبات، بسبب الحركة اليومية محسوس. والدليل عليه: أن الريحان الذي يقال له: النيلوفر، والأذيرون، وورق الخروع، وغيرها فإنها تنمو، وتزداد عند أخذ الشمس في الارتفاع والصعود. فإذا غابت الشمس ضعفت وذبلت.
The eleventh aspect concerning the effect of the sun on plants: and it is in several ways: First: When the sun moves away from the zenith, the cold intensifies in the air, and cold dominates the surface of the earth. Then heat intensifies in the interior of the earth, and there are generated in it the subtle vapors suitable for the formation of minerals, and the splitting of the seed in the belly of the earth. Then when the sun inclines toward the zenith, and the cold disappears, and the air becomes moderate, those fragments come out from the belly of the earth to its surface. Then the air heated by the strength of the sun, the sun affects it. Then ripening and perfection occur in the crops and fruits. Second: The effect of the sun on plants is perceptible due to the daily motion. The evidence for that: that the basil called the water lily (al-nilufar), and al-adhirun, and the castor bean leaves, and others—they grow and increase when the sun rises and ascends. When the sun sets, they weaken and wither.
Source pages p. 340

Commentary
This passage presents the eleventh aspect of the sun's effects on plants, enumerating multiple ways. The first way describes the seasonal mechanism: when the sun is far from the zenith (winter), cold dominates the surface, but heat concentrates in the earth's interior, generating subtle vapors that help form minerals and cause seeds to split. When the sun returns toward the zenith (spring/summer), the fragments emerge, and the heated air brings about ripening of crops and fruits. The second way is the daily effect: the author observes that certain plants like the water lily (nilufar), adhirun (perhaps a type of basil), and castor bean visibly respond to the sun's daily motion—they grow during the day and wither at night. This provides tangible evidence of the sun's direct influence on plant growth.

Key Terms
الحركة اليومية
الريحان
النيلوفر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which plants does the author give as evidence for the daily effect of the sun?
A) Wheat and barley
B) Water lily, adhirun, and castor bean leaves
C) Date palms and olive trees
D) Ferns and mosses

Key Takeaway
Some plants provide clear observable evidence of the sun's daily influence on their growth and wilting.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author says the sun's effect is 'perceptible'—you can see it yourself. When did you last actually look at a plant and notice its response to the sun? What other signs of Allah's care have you allowed to become invisible through routine?
?
If a plant's strength depends on the sun, where do you draw your daily strength from? Are you aware of your own dependence on Allah's constant provision, or do you only notice when the 'sun sets' in your life?
?
The water lily opens and closes with the sun. Your heart too has cycles of openness and hardness. What sun-like source can revive it after the 'sunset' of a sin or neglect? Will you seek that source today?
