The Sun's Necessity for Plant Growth
Author states the third benefit: plant growth requires sunlight.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that, according to the author, plant growth is entirely dependent on the sun's direct rays or its heat.

Core Idea
No plant grows without the sun's influence.

The author continues his enumeration of the benefits of the sun by stating a fundamental observation: plants require sunlight. This seemingly simple point establishes a universal cause for plant life, setting the stage for more specific distributions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once. Notice the concise causal claim.
2
Identify the condition
Identify the condition 'إلا في المواضع التي تطلع عليها الشمس أو يصل إليها قوة حرها'. This is the key restriction.
3
Reflect on implications
Consider why the author begins with this general statement before moving to specific examples.
This establishes the sun as a necessary cause for vegetation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثالثها: إن الزروع والنباتات لا تنمو ولا تنشأ، إلا في المواضع التي تطلع عليها الشمس، أو يصل إليها قوة حرها. ورابعها: إن وجود بعض أنواع النبات في بعض البلاد في الحر والبرد دون البعض، لا سبب له إلا اختلاف البلدان في الحر والبرد، الذي لا سبب له إلا حركة النير الأعظم، فإن النخيل ينبت في البلاد الحارة، ولا ينبت في البلاد الباردة. وكذلك شجر الأترج، والليمون والموز، لا ينبت في البلاد الباردة. وفي الإقليم الأول تنبت الأفاوية الهندية التي لا تنبت في سائر الأقاليم. وفي البلاد الجنوبية التي وراء خط الإستواء تنبت أشجار وفواكه وحشائش، لا يعرف شيء منها في بلاد الشمال. وأما الحيوانات فيختلف الحال في توالدها باختلاف حرارة البلاد وبرودتها، فإن الفيل والعلقم والبير، توجد في أرض الهند، ولا توجد في سائر الأقاليم التي تكون دونها في الحرارة. وكذلك المسك والكركدن. وقد يوجد بعضها في البلاد التي هي حرارة من بلاد الهند، فإن الفيلة توجد في سائر البلدان. حتى في البلاد الجنوبية التي هي بلاد السودان، أعظم جسوماً وأطول أعماراً. وأما انعقاد الأجسام السبعة، والأحجار والمعادن. فمعلوم: أن السبب فيها بخارات تتولد في باطن الأرض بسبب تأثير الشمس. فإذا اختفت تلك البخارات في قصور الجبال، وأثرت الشمس في نضجها، تولدت المعادن. وأما الأمطار وسائر الآثار العلوية، فلا شك في أن تكونها من الأبخرة والأدخنة، ولا شك أن تولدها بقوة الشمس. فلنكتف بهذا القدر من منافع الشمس.
Third: Crops and plants do not grow and develop except in places where the sun rises upon them, or the power of its heat reaches them. Fourth: The existence of some types of plants in some countries, in heat and cold, to the exclusion of others, has no cause except the difference of countries in heat and cold, which has no cause except the movement of the greatest luminary. For date palms grow in hot countries and do not grow in cold countries. Likewise, the citron tree, lemon, and banana do not grow in cold countries. In the first clime, Indian spices grow which do not grow in other climes. And in the southern countries beyond the equator, trees, fruits, and herbs grow that are not known in any of the northern countries. As for animals, the situation regarding their reproduction differs according to the heat and cold of the countries. For the elephant, al-ʻalqam, and al-bayr are found in the land of India, and are not found in the other climes that are below them in heat. Likewise, musk and the rhinoceros. And some of them may be found in countries hotter than India, for elephants are found in other countries, even in the southern lands that are the lands of the Sudan, greater in body and longer in life. As for the formation of the seven bodies, the stones and minerals, it is known that the cause of them is vapors generated inside the earth due to the influence of the sun. When those vapors become confined in mountain caves and the sun affects their maturation, minerals are generated. As for rain and all the high atmospheric effects, there is no doubt that their formation is from vapors and fumes, and there is no doubt that their generation is by the power of the sun. So let us suffice with this amount of the benefits of the sun.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage continues the eleventh aspect, presenting the third and fourth subpoints, then extends to animals, minerals, and rain. The third point states that plants require direct sunlight or its heat to grow. The fourth point argues that the distribution of plant species across different climates—hot vs. cold countries—is caused solely by the sun's movement (the 'greatest luminary'). Examples: date palms, citron, lemon, banana are restricted to hot lands; Indian spices grow only in the first clime; unique plants exist beyond the equator. For animals, the author notes that their reproduction varies with temperature: elephants, 'alqam, and 'bayr' (perhaps elephants, rhinoceros, and other beasts) are found in India, while many are found even larger in hotter Sudan. Minerals form from vapors inside the earth generated by the sun; when trapped in mountain caves and matured by the sun, they become minerals. Rain and atmospheric phenomena also come from vapors and fumes generated by the sun. The author concludes that this suffices to show the benefits of the sun, implying all these are signs of divine wisdom.

Key Terms
الزروع
النباتات
الشمس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for plants to grow?
A) Water only
B) Sunlight or its heat
C) Soil fertility
D) Wind

Key Takeaway
The sun's direct light or heat is indispensable for the growth of all crops and plants.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believed that not a single plant can grow without the sun's direct influence, would you ever again take your food, your oxygen, or your environment for granted? How can you cultivate that awareness today?
?
You depend on the sun every moment, yet you rarely thank its Creator. What would it mean for you to see the sun's warmth not as a given, but as a direct gift from Allah—one that sustains your very life?
?
The author lists this as a simple fact: no growth without the sun. But if you let that fact sink in, it shatters the illusion of self-sufficiency. In what area of your life are you still pretending you can grow without Allah's appointed means?

The Sun's Role in Plant Distribution
Author attributes plant distribution to sun-caused climate differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author attributes the geographic distribution of plant species to differences in heat and cold caused by the sun's movement.

Core Idea
The sun's movement determines which plants grow where.

Building on the general necessity of sunlight, the author now explains that the specific locations of different plant species are due to climatic variations in heat and cold—ultimately caused by the sun. He provides concrete examples from date palms to equatorial spices.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the causal chain: plant distribution → differences in heat/cold → motion of the 'greatest luminary'.
2
Identify the examples
List the plant examples given: date palms, citron, lemon, banana, Indian spices, plants of the southern hemisphere.
These illustrate the principle.
3
Trace the causation
Notice how the author says 'لا سبب له إلا...' to emphasize that the sun is the sole cause of climatic differences.

The Sun's Influence on Animal Distribution
Author argues animal distribution is due to temperature differences caused by the sun.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author connects animal reproduction and distribution to the heat and cold caused by the sun.

Core Idea
Sun-driven climate shapes where animals live and reproduce.

The author now extends the same reasoning to animals: their reproduction and presence vary with temperature, which again traces back to the sun. He gives examples of elephants and other creatures found in hot regions like India and Sudan.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the phrase 'يختلف الحال في توالدها باختلاف حرارة البلاد وبرودتها'.
2
List the animal examples
The author mentions elephant, al-ʻalqam, al-bayr (perhaps rhinoceros or other), musk, and rhinoceros. Note their distributions.
3
Observe the comparison
Notice that some animals are unique to India, while others (like elephants) are found even in hotter Sudan, with larger bodies.

The Sun's Role in Mineral Formation
Author explains mineral formation via sun-generated vapors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the mechanism by which the author explains mineral formation as resulting from solar-generated vapors.

Core Idea
Minerals are formed from sun-generated vapors trapped underground.

The author now turns to minerals and stones, explaining their origins not in the earth itself but in vapors created by the sun's heat. He describes a process: vapors generated inside the earth become confined in mountain caves, and the sun's influence 'matures' them into minerals.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the cause-effect relationship: sun → vapors → confinement → minerals.
2
Identify the process
Break down the process: (1) sun's influence generates vapors inside earth, (2) vapors become confined in mountain caves, (3) sun's effect matures them into minerals.
3
Reflect on the term 'انعقاد'
Notice the word 'انعقاد' (formation/coagulation), which implies a solidification process.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثالثها: إن الزروع والنباتات لا تنمو ولا تنشأ، إلا في المواضع التي تطلع عليها الشمس، أو يصل إليها قوة حرها. ورابعها: إن وجود بعض أنواع النبات في بعض البلاد في الحر والبرد دون البعض، لا سبب له إلا اختلاف البلدان في الحر والبرد، الذي لا سبب له إلا حركة النير الأعظم، فإن النخيل ينبت في البلاد الحارة، ولا ينبت في البلاد الباردة. وكذلك شجر الأترج، والليمون والموز، لا ينبت في البلاد الباردة. وفي الإقليم الأول تنبت الأفاوية الهندية التي لا تنبت في سائر الأقاليم. وفي البلاد الجنوبية التي وراء خط الإستواء تنبت أشجار وفواكه وحشائش، لا يعرف شيء منها في بلاد الشمال. وأما الحيوانات فيختلف الحال في توالدها باختلاف حرارة البلاد وبرودتها، فإن الفيل والعلقم والبير، توجد في أرض الهند، ولا توجد في سائر الأقاليم التي تكون دونها في الحرارة. وكذلك المسك والكركدن. وقد يوجد بعضها في البلاد التي هي حرارة من بلاد الهند، فإن الفيلة توجد في سائر البلدان. حتى في البلاد الجنوبية التي هي بلاد السودان، أعظم جسوماً وأطول أعماراً. وأما انعقاد الأجسام السبعة، والأحجار والمعادن. فمعلوم: أن السبب فيها بخارات تتولد في باطن الأرض بسبب تأثير الشمس. فإذا اختفت تلك البخارات في قصور الجبال، وأثرت الشمس في نضجها، تولدت المعادن. وأما الأمطار وسائر الآثار العلوية، فلا شك في أن تكونها من الأبخرة والأدخنة، ولا شك أن تولدها بقوة الشمس. فلنكتف بهذا القدر من منافع الشمس.
Third: Crops and plants do not grow and develop except in places where the sun rises upon them, or the power of its heat reaches them. Fourth: The existence of some types of plants in some countries, in heat and cold, to the exclusion of others, has no cause except the difference of countries in heat and cold, which has no cause except the movement of the greatest luminary. For date palms grow in hot countries and do not grow in cold countries. Likewise, the citron tree, lemon, and banana do not grow in cold countries. In the first clime, Indian spices grow which do not grow in other climes. And in the southern countries beyond the equator, trees, fruits, and herbs grow that are not known in any of the northern countries. As for animals, the situation regarding their reproduction differs according to the heat and cold of the countries. For the elephant, al-ʻalqam, and al-bayr are found in the land of India, and are not found in the other climes that are below them in heat. Likewise, musk and the rhinoceros. And some of them may be found in countries hotter than India, for elephants are found in other countries, even in the southern lands that are the lands of the Sudan, greater in body and longer in life. As for the formation of the seven bodies, the stones and minerals, it is known that the cause of them is vapors generated inside the earth due to the influence of the sun. When those vapors become confined in mountain caves and the sun affects their maturation, minerals are generated. As for rain and all the high atmospheric effects, there is no doubt that their formation is from vapors and fumes, and there is no doubt that their generation is by the power of the sun. So let us suffice with this amount of the benefits of the sun.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage continues the eleventh aspect, presenting the third and fourth subpoints, then extends to animals, minerals, and rain. The third point states that plants require direct sunlight or its heat to grow. The fourth point argues that the distribution of plant species across different climates—hot vs. cold countries—is caused solely by the sun's movement (the 'greatest luminary'). Examples: date palms, citron, lemon, banana are restricted to hot lands; Indian spices grow only in the first clime; unique plants exist beyond the equator. For animals, the author notes that their reproduction varies with temperature: elephants, 'alqam, and 'bayr' (perhaps elephants, rhinoceros, and other beasts) are found in India, while many are found even larger in hotter Sudan. Minerals form from vapors inside the earth generated by the sun; when trapped in mountain caves and matured by the sun, they become minerals. Rain and atmospheric phenomena also come from vapors and fumes generated by the sun. The author concludes that this suffices to show the benefits of the sun, implying all these are signs of divine wisdom.

Key Terms
الأجسام السبعة
المعادن
البخارات
قصور الجبال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Minerals are formed directly from earth or by chance.
Correction: The author asserts minerals are formed from vapors generated by the sun and matured in confined spaces.

Checkpoint
What happens to the vapors before minerals are formed?
A) They escape into the atmosphere
B) They are confined in mountain caves
C) They combine with water
D) They cool rapidly

Key Takeaway
Minerals are formed when sun-generated vapors become trapped in mountain caves and are matured by the sun.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hold a rock or mineral, do you ever reflect on the intricate, hidden process Allah designed for its formation—from the sun's heat to the vapors to the caves? How does this awareness affect your sense of wonder at His creation?
?
This lesson shows that even the 'lifeless' mineral world follows a deliberate, causal process. If Allah is so precise in forming rocks, what does that tell you about His care in shaping your own life, especially during times when His work seems hidden?
?
The sun, a constant and seemingly ordinary part of your day, plays a vital role in forming minerals deep underground. What other everyday blessings of Allah do you overlook? Will you commit today to actively noticing one such blessing and thanking Him for it?

The Sun's Role in Rain and Atmospheric Effects
Author attributes rain and atmospheric effects to sun-generated vapors.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author attributes rain and other atmospheric phenomena to vapors and fumes generated by the sun's power.

Core Idea
Rain and weather are products of sun-powered vapors.

In the final part of this passage, the author extends the sun's causal role to atmospheric phenomena. He asserts without doubt that rain and all high atmospheric effects originate from vapors and fumes (الأبخرة والأدخنة), which are generated by the sun's power. He then closes this section on the sun's benefits.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation, noting the emphatic phrase 'لا شك في أن تكونها من الأبخرة والأدخنة'.
2
Identify the phenomenon
Rain and other atmospheric effects are attributed to vapors and fumes.
3
Note the conclusion
The author ends with 'فلنكتف بهذا القدر من منافع الشمس', indicating this is a summary of the sun's benefits.

Second Argument: Sun's Daily Motion and Plant Growth
Second argument: sun's daily motion affects plants observably

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the second argument uses observable plant behavior to demonstrate the sun's causal influence.

Core Idea
Plants respond to the sun's daily motion, proving its causal role.

The second argument focuses on a simple, everyday observation: certain plants open and grow with the sunrise and wither at sunset. This direct correlation provides a clear evidence for the sun's effect on plant life, grounded in the sun's daily motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the argument's structure. Notice the specific plants mentioned.
2
Identify the evidence
Look for the examples of plants that respond to the sun's daily motion. Understand the correlation: growth with sunrise, wilting with sunset.
The plants named are the lotus (nilufar), adharyun, and castor leaves.
3
Understand the logic
The argument uses a cause-and-effect relationship: the sun's rising and setting directly correlates with plant growth and decline, illustrating a causal link.
4
Reflect on the broader context
Consider how this argument fits into the larger discussion of the sun's benefits within a theological framework, showing God's design through natural causes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثانيها : إن تأثير الشمس في النبات ، بسبب الحركة اليومية ليومية محسوس . والدليل عليه : أن الريحان الذي يقال له : النيلوفر ، والأذيرون ، وورق الخروع، وغيرها فإنها تنمو ، وتزداد عند أخذ الشمس في الارتفاع والصعود . فإذا غابت الشمس ضعفت وذبلت
وثالثها : إن الزروع والنباتات لا تنمو ولا تنشأ ، إلا في المواضع التي تطلع عليها الشمس ، أو يصل إليها قوة حرها
ورابعها : إن وجود بعض أنواع النبات في بعض البلاد في الحر والبرد دون البعض ، لا سبب له إلا اختلاف البلدان في الحر والبرد ، الذي لا سبب له إلا حركة النير الأعظم، فإن النخيل ينبت في البلاد الحارة ، ولا ينبت في البلاد الباردة . وكذلك شجر الأترج ، والليمون والموز ، لا ينبت في البلاد الباردة . وفي الإقليم الأول تنبت الأفاوية الهندية التي لا تنبت في سائر الأقاليم. وفي البلاد الجنوبية التي وراء خط الإستواء تنبت أشجار وفواكه وحشائش ، لا يعرف شيء منها في بلاد الشمال . وأما الحيوانات فيختلف الحال في توالدها باختلاف حرارة البلاد برودتها ، فإن الفيل والعلقم والبير ، توجد في أرض الهند ، ولا توجد في سائر الأقاليم التي تكون دونها في الحرارة. وكذلك المسك والكركدن . وقد يوجد بعضها في البلاد التي هي حرارة من بلاد الهند ، فإن الفيلة توجد في سائر البلدان . حتى في البلاد الجنوبية التي هي بلاد السودان ، أعظم جسوماً وأطول أعماراً . وأما انعقاد الأجسام السبعة ، والأحجار والمعادن. فمعلوم : أن السبب فيها بخارات تتولد في باطن الأرض بسبب تأثير الشمس . فإذا اختفت تلك البخارات في قصور الجبال ، وأثرت الشمس في نضجها ، تولدت المعادن . وأما الأمطار وسائر الآثار العلوية ، فلا شك في أن تكونها من الأبخرة والأدخنة ، ولا شك أن تولدها بقوة الشمس
فلنكتف بهذا القدر من منافع الشمس .
The second: The effect of the sun on plants is due to the daily motion, which is perceptible. The evidence for it is that the basil called the lotus, and the adharyun, and the leaves of castor oil plant, and others, they grow and increase when the sun begins to rise and ascend. So when the sun sets, they become weak and wither. The third: Crops and plants do not grow and develop except in places where the sun rises upon them, or the power of its heat reaches them. The fourth: The existence of some types of plants in some countries in heat and cold to the exclusion of others has no cause except the difference of countries in heat and cold, which has no cause except the motion of the great luminary. For palm trees grow in hot countries and do not grow in cold countries. Likewise the citron tree, lemon, and banana do not grow in cold countries. In the first climate, Indian spices grow which do not grow in other climates. And in the southern countries beyond the equator, trees, fruits, and herbs grow, none of which are known in the northern countries. As for animals, the condition of their reproduction varies with the heat and cold of the countries. For the elephant, the 'alqam, and the peer exist in the land of India and do not exist in other climates that are below it in heat. Likewise musk and the rhinoceros. And some of them are found in countries that are hotter than India, for elephants are found in other countries, even in the southern countries which are the countries of the Sudan, they are greater in size and longer in lifespan. As for the formation of the seven bodies, stones, and minerals, it is known that the cause of them is vapors that are generated in the interior of the earth due to the effect of the sun. So when those vapors are confined in the hollows of mountains, and the sun effects their ripening, minerals are generated. As for rain and other celestial effects, there is no doubt that they are formed from vapors and fumes, and there is no doubt that their generation is by the power of the sun. Let us suffice with this amount of the benefits of the sun.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage presents four arguments (the second, third, fourth, and an extended argument about animals and minerals) to demonstrate the sun's causal influence on earthly phenomena. The author begins with the second argument, stating that the sun's daily motion causes perceptible effects on plants, giving examples like the lotus and castor leaves that grow with the sun and wither at sunset. The third argument notes that plants only grow where sunlight reaches. The fourth argument correlates plant distribution with temperature, attributing temperature differences to the motion of the great luminary (the sun). The author then extends the argument to animals, noting that species like elephants are found only in hot regions, and size may increase with heat. Finally, the formation of minerals through vapors and rain through evaporation is attributed to the sun's power. The passage concludes by saying this suffices for the benefits of the sun. The structure follows an enumeration of points, though the first argument is missing from this window.

Key Terms
الشمس
النبات
الحركة اليومية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The sun's effect on plants is indirect or not due to daily motion.
Correction: The argument uses direct observation to show a clear, immediate causal link between the sun's rising and setting and plant behavior.

Checkpoint
According to the second argument, what happens to plants like the lotus when the sun sets?
A) They grow faster
B) They become weak and wither
C) They produce fruit
D) They change color

Key Takeaway
The second argument uses observable plant responses to the sun's daily motion as direct evidence of the sun's causal influence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness the daily rising and setting of the sun, do you ever pause to consider that the plants around you are literally responding to that motion? What would it mean for your faith if you saw this as a direct sign from the Creator rather than just a natural routine?
?
The passage says that certain plants grow when the sun rises and wither when it sets. Think of a habit or attitude in your life that flourishes in the 'light' of awareness of God but withers in neglect. What is it, and what will you do today to keep it in the sun?
?
If the sun's motion is a clear, perceptible cause of life and death in plants, how can you ignore the even clearer signs of God's power and mercy in your own life? What sign have you been overlooking that demands your gratitude or repentance right now?

Third Argument: Plants Require Sunlight to Grow
Third argument: plants need sunlight to grow

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the third argument, which establishes that plants only grow in places reached by sunlight.

Core Idea
Plants cannot grow without sunlight – a universal observation.

The third argument is a straightforward generalization: crops and plants only grow where sunlight reaches. This common-sense observation reinforces the sun's essential role in plant life.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the very brief third argument. It is a single sentence in Arabic.
2
Understand the claim
The claim is universal: plants do not grow except in places where the sun rises upon them or its heat reaches them.
3
Connect to experience
Relate this to your own knowledge: think of shaded areas vs. sunny spots. This is a basic rule of agriculture.

The second: The effect of the sun on plants is due to the daily motion, which is perceptible. The evidence for it is that the basil called the lotus, and the adharyun, and the leaves of castor oil plant, and others, they grow and increase when the sun begins to rise and ascend. So when the sun sets, they become weak and wither. The third: Crops and plants do not grow and develop except in places where the sun rises upon them, or the power of its heat reaches them. The fourth: The existence of some types of plants in some countries in heat and cold to the exclusion of others has no cause except the difference of countries in heat and cold, which has no cause except the motion of the great luminary. For palm trees grow in hot countries and do not grow in cold countries. Likewise the citron tree, lemon, and banana do not grow in cold countries. In the first climate, Indian spices grow which do not grow in other climates. And in the southern countries beyond the equator, trees, fruits, and herbs grow, none of which are known in the northern countries. As for animals, the condition of their reproduction varies with the heat and cold of the countries. For the elephant, the 'alqam, and the peer exist in the land of India and do not exist in other climates that are below it in heat. Likewise musk and the rhinoceros. And some of them are found in countries that are hotter than India, for elephants are found in other countries, even in the southern countries which are the countries of the Sudan, they are greater in size and longer in lifespan. As for the formation of the seven bodies, stones, and minerals, it is known that the cause of them is vapors that are generated in the interior of the earth due to the effect of the sun. So when those vapors are confined in the hollows of mountains, and the sun effects their ripening, minerals are generated. As for rain and other celestial effects, there is no doubt that they are formed from vapors and fumes, and there is no doubt that their generation is by the power of the sun. Let us suffice with this amount of the benefits of the sun.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage presents four arguments (the second, third, fourth, and an extended argument about animals and minerals) to demonstrate the sun's causal influence on earthly phenomena. The author begins with the second argument, stating that the sun's daily motion causes perceptible effects on plants, giving examples like the lotus and castor leaves that grow with the sun and wither at sunset. The third argument notes that plants only grow where sunlight reaches. The fourth argument correlates plant distribution with temperature, attributing temperature differences to the motion of the great luminary (the sun). The author then extends the argument to animals, noting that species like elephants are found only in hot regions, and size may increase with heat. Finally, the formation of minerals through vapors and rain through evaporation is attributed to the sun's power. The passage concludes by saying this suffices for the benefits of the sun. The structure follows an enumeration of points, though the first argument is missing from this window.

Fourth Argument: Climate Diversity Explained by Sun's Motion
Fourth argument: plant distribution due to sun's motion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the fourth argument uses plant distribution across climates to demonstrate the sun's causal role.

Core Idea
Plant distribution across hot and cold regions traces back to the sun's motion.

The fourth argument examines why certain plants exist only in specific climates. It attributes this to differences in heat and cold, which are ultimately caused by the motion of the great luminary (the sun). Examples include palm trees in hot countries and citrus fruits in warm regions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully. It lists examples of plants that grow only in hot or cold regions.
2
Identify the causal chain
Note the chain: plant distribution → climate differences → sun's motion. The sun is the ultimate cause.
3
Understand the examples
Palm trees, citron, lemon, banana prefer hot regions. Indian spices grow only in the first climate. Southern equatorial regions have unique plants.

The second: The effect of the sun on plants is due to the daily motion, which is perceptible. Sun's Influence on Animals, Minerals, and Rain
Sun's effects on animals, minerals, and rain

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the sun's causal influence extends beyond plants to animals, mineral formation, and rain.

Core Idea
The sun's power shapes animal habitats, mineral deposits, and the water cycle.

After discussing plants, the author extends the argument to animals, noting that their reproduction varies with temperature, and provides examples like elephants in hot regions. He then explains mineral formation through vapors heated by the sun, and rain as a result of evaporation by the sun's power.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on animals

2
Understand mineral formation
Read the explanation that minerals form from vapors in the earth, activated by the sun's heat. The vapors condense in mountains and 'ripen' into metals.
3
Understand rain formation
Rain and other atmospheric phenomena are formed from vapors and fumes, which are generated by the sun's power.
4
Synthesize the overall argument
Recognize that the sun's influence is universal: it affects plants, animals, minerals, and weather.

The Moon's Influence on Moisture and Tides
The author contrasts the moon's influence with the sun's and gives tidal evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the moon influences moisture and tides through its phases, based on the author's empirical evidence.

Core Idea
The moon, though smaller, governs moisture and tides through its phases.

The author begins by asserting the moon's independent influence on the sublunary world, despite its smaller size. He contrasts its effect with the sun's: the sun governs heat and cold, while the moon governs moisture and dryness. He then provides the first of several evidences from tidal observations.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the contrast between sun and moon effects.
2
Understand the contrast
Identify the sun's role in heat/cold and the moon's role in moisture/dryness. Note that the author explains how distance and phases cause these effects.
3
Examine the tidal evidence
The author presents the first type of evidence from tidal observations. Observe how the seas increase and decrease with the moon's phases.
The passage cuts off mid-sentence, so this evidence is incomplete.

الفصل الثاني
اعلم : أن القمر لا نسبة له إلى الشمس في كبر الجسم ، وقوة التأثير البتة . إلا أن له أيضاً قوة عظيمة في التأثير في هذا العالم

Chapter Two
Know: The moon has no proportion to the sun in size of body and strength of effect at all. However, it also has a great power of effect in this world. The people of verification said: The effect of the sun on heat and cold is more apparent, and the effect of the moon on moisture and dryness is stronger. And our statement: 'The sun affects heat and cold' means that when it is near it gives heat, and when it is distant it gives cold. Similarly is the case of the moon with moisture and dryness. And what indicates what we have mentioned are types: The first type: The people of experience said: Among the seas, some begin to increase from the time the moon departs from the sun until the time of fullness. Then they begin to decrease after fullness, and that decrease continues according to the decrease of the moonlight until it reaches the utmost decrease at the occurrence of the new moon, then it begins to increase again as in the first cycle. And among the seas, some occur...
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage introduces the moon's independent influence on the sublunary world, despite its smaller size and lesser power compared to the sun. The author quotes 'the people of verification' to establish that while the sun dominates heat and cold, the moon dominates moisture and dryness. He then explains his terminology: the sun's nearness gives heat, distance gives cold; similarly, the moon's phases affect moisture and dryness. The evidence for this is presented in types, of which only the first is given here. This first type is empirical: tidal observations show that the seas increase from the time the moon separates from the sun until full moon, then decrease until the new moon, and then increase again in a cycle. The passage cuts off before completing the types. The argument relies on observed correlation to prove causal influence.

The Moon's Effect on Tides
Classification of lunar tidal effects with empirical evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the moon's causal influence on tides as presented by the author, including both monthly and daily cycles, and the empirical evidence cited.

Core Idea
The moon drives both monthly and daily tides through its changing position.

This passage presents the moon's effect on tides as a clear example of causation in the physical world. The author first acknowledges the moon's lesser influence compared to the sun, then details empirical evidence from monthly cycles and daily rhythms. By reading this, you'll see how classical scholars integrated observation and reasoning to explain natural phenomena.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the full Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the literal translation to grasp the author's description.
Notice the author's systematic approach: first a general statement, then a classification, then detailed evidence.
2
Identify the two types of tidal effects
The passage presents two sub-parts under 'the first type'. Find the monthly cycle (from new moon to full moon) and the daily cycle (linked to rising and setting).
The monthly cycle is based on the moon's light increase/decrease; the daily cycle is based on the moon's position in the sky.
3
Follow the description of the daily cycle
Trace the daily tidal cycle as described: when the moon rises, the sea flows until the moon reaches the meridian, then ebbs until setting, then flows again until nadir, then ebbs again.
The author uses 'peg of the earth' for the nadir opposite the zenith.
4
Note the practical indicators for sailors and coastal dwellers
The author gives signs for sailors (swelling, storms) and coastal dwellers (vertical water movement). This shows how the theory connects to observation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني
اعلم : أن القمر لا نسبة له إلى الشمس في كبر الجسم ، وقوة التأثير البتة . إلا أن له [ أيضاً (۱) ] قوة عظيمة في التأثير في هذا العالم
قال أهل التحقيق : تأثير الشمس في الحر والبرد أظهر . وتأثير القمر في الرطوبة والجفاف أقوى . وقولنا : « الشمس تؤثر في الحرارة والبرودة » : نعني به : أنها عند القرب تفيد الحرارة ، وعند البعد تفيد البرودة . وكذا حال القمر مع الرطوبة والجفاف
والذي يدل على ما ذكرناه أنواع (۲) : النوع الأول (۳) ] : أن أصحاب التجارب : [ قـالوا ) ] : إن من البحار ما يأخذ في الازدياد من حين يفارق القمر الشمس ، إلى وقت الامتلاء . ثم إنها تأخذ في الانتقاص بعد الامتلاء ، ولا يزال يستمر ذلك الانتقاص بحسب نقصان نور القمر ، حتى ينتهي إلى غاية نقصانه عند حصول المحاق ، ثم يأخذ في الازدياد مرة أخرى كما في الدور [ الأول (٥) ] ومن البحار ما يحصل
فيه المد والجزر في كل يوم وليلة ، مع طلوع القمر وغروبه . وذلك موجود في بحر فارس وبحر الهند . وكذلك أيضاً في بحر الصين . وكيفيته : أنه إذا بلغ القمر مشرقاً من مشارق البحر ، ابتدأ البحر بالمد ، ولا يزال كذلك إلى أن يصير القمر إلى وسط سماء ذلك الموضع ، فعند ذلك يبلغ المد منتهاه . فإذا انحط القمر من وسط ذلك الموضع ، جزر الماء ورجع إلى البحر . ولا يزال كذلك راجعاً إلى أن يبلغ مغربه (۱) ، فعند ذلك ينتهي الجزر منتهاه . فإذا زال القمر من مغرب ذلك الموضع ، ابتدأ المد هناك في المرة الثانية ، ولا يزال زائداً إلى أن يصل القمر إلى وتد الأرض ، فحينئذ ينتهي المد منتهاه في المرة الثانية . ثم يبتدىء الجزر ثانيا ويرجع الماء إلى البحر، حتى يبلغ القمر أفق ذلك الموضع، فتعود الحالة المذكورة مرة أخرى. ولأن الأرض مستديرة ، والبحر محيط بها على استدارتها ، والقمر يطلع [ عليها (۲) ] كلها في مقدار اليوم والليلة . فكلما تحرك القمر قوساً ، صار موضع القمر أفقاً لموضع آخر ، من مواضع البحر وصار (۳) ذلك الموضع وسط سماء الموضع آخر ومغرباً لموضع آخر ، ووند الأرض لموضع آخر. وفيما بين كل وتد من هذه الأوتاد ، تحصل أحوال اخرى . فلا جرم يحصل لأجل هذه الأسباب ، أحوال مختلفة مضطربة في البحر
واعلم : أن سكان البحر كلما رأوا في البحر انتفاخاً وهيجان رياح عاصفة ، وأمواج شديدة : علموا : أنه ابتدأ المد . وإذا ذهب الانتفاخ ، وقلت الأمواج والرياح : علموا : أنه وقت الجزر. وأما أصحاب الشطوط والسواحل ، فإنهم يجدون عندهم في وقت المد للماء : حركة من أسفله إلى أعلاه . فإذا رجع الماء ، ونزل فهناك وقت الجزر .
The Second Chapter
Know that the moon has absolutely no proportion to the sun in terms of body size and strength of effect. However, it also has a great power of influence in this world.
The investigators said: The sun's effect in heat and cold is more apparent, and the moon's effect in moisture and dryness is stronger. And our saying, 'The sun influences heat and coldness,' we mean by it that when it is near it produces heat, and when it is far it produces coldness. The same holds for the moon with moisture and dryness.
That which indicates what we have mentioned is of types (2): The first type: The experimentalists said: Among the seas, there are those that begin to increase from the time the moon separates from the sun until the time of fullness [full moon]. Then they begin to decrease after fullness, and that decrease continues according to the decrease of the moon's light until it reaches the utmost of its decrease at the time of conjunction, then it begins to increase again as in the first cycle. And among the seas, there are those in which ebb and flow occur every day and night, with the rising and setting of the moon. That exists in the Persian Sea and the Indian Sea, and also in the Chinese Sea. Its description: When the moon reaches a rising point of the sea, the sea begins to flow, and it continues thus until the moon reaches the middle of the sky of that place; then the flow reaches its maximum. When the moon descends from the middle of that place, the water ebbs and returns to the sea, and it continues returning until it reaches its setting; then the ebb reaches its maximum. When the moon departs from the setting of that place, the flow begins there a second time, and it continues increasing until the moon reaches the 'peg of the earth' (the nadir), then the flow reaches its maximum in the second time. Then the ebb begins a second time and the water returns to the sea until the moon reaches the horizon of that place, so the mentioned state returns again. And because the earth is spherical, and the sea surrounds it on its sphericity, and the moon rises upon all of it in the span of a day and night. So whenever the moon moves an arc, the moon's position becomes the horizon for another position of the sea, and that position becomes the middle of the sky for another position, and a setting for another position, and the peg of the earth for another position. And between each of these pegs, other states occur. Therefore, due to these causes, various and confused states occur in the sea.
And know that the inhabitants of the sea, whenever they see in the sea swelling, violent stormy winds, and strong waves, they know that the flow has begun. And when the swelling disappears, and the waves and winds lessen, they know that it is the time of ebb. As for the inhabitants of the banks and coasts, they find at their places at the time of the flow a movement of the water from its bottom to its top. When the water returns and descends, then that is the time of ebb.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a scientific classification and proof of the moon's effects on the physical world. The author begins by acknowledging the moon's inferiority to the sun in size and strength, yet affirms its great influence. He then cites the opinion of investigators: the sun primarily affects temperature (heat and cold), while the moon primarily affects moisture and dryness. This sets up the moon's role in hydrological phenomena. The evidence is presented in two types: The first type describes seasonal tidal variations corresponding to the lunar month: seas increase from the moon's separation from the sun (new moon) to fullness (full moon), then decrease. This is a monthly cycle. The second part of the first type describes daily tides linked to the moon's rising and setting, observed in the Persian, Indian, and Chinese seas. The author gives a detailed account of the daily cycle: when the moon rises, the sea flows until the moon reaches the meridian, then ebbs until moonset, then flows again until the moon reaches the nadir ('peg of the earth'), then ebbs again until moonrise. He explains that since the earth is spherical and the sea surrounds it, and the moon rises over all parts in a day and night, every motion of the moon creates different tidal states for different locations. Finally, he notes practical indicators: sailors observe swelling and rough seas at the beginning of flow, while shore dwellers perceive vertical movement of water. The passage thus provides empirical and rational evidence for the moon's causal influence on tides.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the moon only affects tides during full moon.
Correction: The passage shows both monthly (linked to lunar phase) and daily (linked to moon's position) cycles are tied to the moon's influence.

Checkpoint

A) Seasonal and daily tides
B) Spring and neap tides
C) High and low tides

Key Takeaway
The moon's position relative to a location determines the state of the tide, producing both monthly and daily cycles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

In your own spiritual life, are you like the sailor—attuned to deeper signs of change—or like the shore dweller, only noticing when things are already shifting? What would it take for you to become more aware of the subtle signs of Allah's guidance in your daily life?

Does it vary like the tide? Or are you striving for consistency in worship, knowing that Allah's patterns in creation are precise and unchanging?
?
The investigators observed the moon's effect through empirical evidence. How often do you reflect on the natural world as a means to strengthen your faith? Are you living as if the universe is a book of signs, or do you only look for evidence of Allah in ritual worship? Commit today to observe one natural phenomenon this week and consciously connect it to Allah's power and wisdom.

The Moon's Effect on Animal Bodies
States the second type of the moon's effect: it strengthens animal bodies when its light increases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the claim that the moon's phases directly influence the strength and temperature of animal bodies.

Core Idea
The moon's light strength directly affects animal bodies.

This lesson presents a specific claim about the moon's influence on living creatures. The author states that as the moon's light increases, animal bodies become stronger and hotter, and after the full moon they weaken and cool. This is part of a broader argument for the moon's causal power beyond just tidal effects on water.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the two distinct phases described.
Pay attention to the terminology 'increase of light' and 'after full moon'.
2
Identify the two phases
Find the two time periods mentioned: when the moon's light is increasing, and after it is full. Note the contrasting effects.
3
Reflect on the causal claim
Consider what this claims about the moon's power. Does it make sense? How might one test it?
This is a simple empirical observation.

The second type of the effects of the moon: The bodies of animals at the time of increase of the moon's light are stronger and hotter, and after the full moon they are weaker and colder.

This passage presents the second type of the moon's effects, focusing on animal bodies. The author asserts that when the moon's light increases (i.e., from new moon to full moon), animal bodies become stronger and hotter, and after the full moon (when the light decreases), they become weaker and colder. This is a brief empirical claim about the moon's influence on living organisms, complementing the earlier discussion of its effects on the inanimate world (seas). The claim is stated without further proof in this excerpt, but it is offered as part of the overall argument for the moon's power.

Six Types of Lunar Influence on Earthly Phenomena
Razi enumerates types of lunar influence on humors, crises, hair, milk, brains, etc.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the six categories of observable lunar influence on earthly phenomena as catalogued by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi, and how he uses induction to support his argument.

Core Idea
The moon's phases systematically affect humors, plants, animals, and even minerals.

Fakhr al-Din al-Razi presents an extensive empirical catalog of lunar influences on the sublunar world. This passage enumerates six types of observed correlations between the moon's light and various biological and physical phenomena. As you read, note how al-Razi moves from human humors to animals, plants, and minerals, always tying his observations to the moon's waxing and waning.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Begin by reading the entire Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the six types of lunar influence. Don't worry about details at this stage.
This is a long passage; take your time.
2
Identify the six types
The passage explicitly lists 'the third type', 'the fourth type', 'the fifth type', and 'the sixth type'. Note that the first two types appear to be missing from this excerpt, but we can infer them from context. List each type and its key observations.
The text also includes sub-observations within each type.
3
Examine the method of induction
Notice that al-Razi repeatedly uses the phrase 'through induction' and gives specific examples. Consider how he uses empirical evidence to support the causal claim that the moon influences earthly phenomena.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider what this enumeration tells us about al-Razi's worldview and the connection between celestial and terrestrial realms. Is he making a claim about causation or merely correlation?
This connects to broader debates in Islamic philosophy about causation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتكون الأخلاط التي في بدن الإنسان ما دام القمر زائداً في ضوئه، فإنها تكون أزيد. ويكون ظاهر البدن أكثر رطوبة وحسناً، فإذا انقص ضوء القمر، صارت هذه الأخلاط في غور البدن والعروق، وازداد ظاهر البدن يبساً. والنوع الثالث: اختلاف أحوال البحرانات، وتفاوت أيامها، وكل ذلك مبني على زيادة نور القمر ونقصانه. والنوع الرابع: شعر الحيوان. فإنه ما دام القمر زائداً في ضوئه، يسرع نباته ويغلظ ويكثر. فإذا أخذ ضوء القمر في الانتقاص، أبطأ نباته ولم يغلظ. وأيضاً: ألبان الحيوانات في أول الشهر إلى نصفه، ما دام القمر زائداً في الضوء، فإذا نقص ضوء القمر نقصت غزارتها. وكذلك أيضاً: أدمغة الحيوانات، تكون زائدة في أول الشهر، عما في آخره. وكذا القول في بياض البيض. ثم قالوا: بل هذه الأحوال تختلف بسبب اختلاف حال القمر في اليوم الواحد. فإن القمر إذا كان فوق الأرض في الربع الشرقي، فإنه تكثر ألبان الضروع، وتزداد أدمغة الحيوانات. فإذا زال القمر وغاب عنهم، نقص نقصاناً ظاهراً. وهذه الاعتبارات تظهر عند الاستقراء، ظهوراً بيناً. ومما يقوي ذلك: أن الإنسان، إذا قعد أو نام في ضوء القمر، حدث في بدنه الاسترخاء والكسل، وتهيج عليه الزكام والصداع، وإذا وضعت لحوم الحيوانات مكشوفة تحت ضوء القمر، تغيرت طعومها وروائحها. والنوع الخامس: إنه يوجد السمك في البحار والأجام والمياه الجارية. وإذا كان من أول الشهر إلى الامتلاء. فإنها تخرج من قعور الأجام والبحار، ويكون سمنها أزيد. وأما من بعد الامتلاء إلى الاجتماع فإنها تدخل في القعور وينقص سمنها. وأما في اليوم بليلته، فما دام القمر مقبلاً من المشرق إلى وسط السماء، فإنها تخرج سمينة، فإذا زال القمر عادت في أجحرتها، ولا تكون في غاية السمن. وكذلك أيضاً هوام الأرض يكون خروجها من أجحرتها في النصف الأول من الشهر، أكثر من خروجها في النصف الثاني. والنوع السادس: إن الأشجار والغروس إذا غرست، والقمر زائد الضوء ومقبل إلى وسط السماء: قويت وكثرت ونشأت وحملت النبات. وإن كان ناقصاً في الضوء زائلاً عن وسط السماء، كان بالضد. وكذا القول في الرياحين والبقول والأعشاب، فإنها تكون أزيد نشوءاً ونمواً إذا كان القمر من الاجتماع إلى الامتلاء. وأما في النصف الثاني من الشهر، فالحال بالضد من ذلك. والقرع والقثاء والخيار والبطيخ ينمو نمواً بالغاً عند ازدياد الضوء، فأما وسط الشهر عند فصول الامتلاء، فهناك يعظم النمو، حتى أنه يظهر التفاوت في الحس في الليلة الواحدة. وكذلك المعادن والينابيع. فإنها تزداد في النصف الأول من الشهر، وتنقص في النصف الثاني منه. وذلك معروف عند أصحاب المعادن. واعلم: أن القمر إنما كان قوي التأثير في هذا العالم لثلاثة أوجه:
And the humors that are in the body of man, as long as the moon is increasing in its light, they are more. And the exterior of the body is more moist and handsome. So when the light of the moon decreases, these humors go into the depth of the body and the veins, and the exterior of the body increases in dryness. The third type: the variation of the states of crises, and the differences of their days, and all that is based on the increase and decrease of the light of the moon. The fourth type: the hair of animals. For as long as the moon is increasing in its light, its growth is rapid, and it becomes coarse and abundant. So when the light of the moon begins to decrease, its growth slows and it does not become coarse. And also: the milk of animals from the beginning of the month to its middle, as long as the moon is increasing in light; so when the light of the moon decreases, its abundance decreases. And likewise also: the brains of animals are more at the beginning of the month than at its end. And the same applies to egg whites. Then they said: Rather these states vary due to the variation of the state of the moon in a single day. For when the moon is above the earth in the eastern quadrant, then the milk of the udders multiplies, and the brains of animals increase. So when the moon sets and disappears from them, they decrease with a clear decrease. And these considerations become manifest through induction, with clear manifestation. And what strengthens that: when a person sits or sleeps in the moonlight, relaxation and laziness occur in his body, and catarrh and headache are stirred up against him. And if animal meats are placed exposed under moonlight, their tastes and odors change. The fifth type: fish are found in the seas, lagoons, and running waters. And from the beginning of the month to the full moon, they come out from the bottoms of the lagoons and seas, and their fat is greater. As for after the full moon to the conjunction, they enter into the bottoms and their fat decreases. As for the day with its night, as long as the moon is coming from the east to the middle of the sky, they come out fat; so when the moon sets, they return to their burrows, and they are not at the peak of fatness. And likewise also the insects of the earth: their emergence from their burrows in the first half of the month is more than their emergence in the second half. The sixth type: trees and saplings, when planted while the moon is increasing in light and approaching the middle of the sky, become strong, multiply, grow, and bear fruit. But if it is decreasing in light and moving away from the middle of the sky, the opposite is the case. And the same applies to aromatic plants, legumes, and herbs, for they are more in growth and development when the moon is from conjunction to full moon. As for the second half of the month, the situation is the opposite. And gourd, cucumber, cucumber, and watermelon grow extremely with the increase of light; at the middle of the month at the times of full moon, growth becomes great, so much so that the difference is perceptible in a single night. And likewise minerals and springs: they increase in the first half of the month and decrease in the second half. And that is known among miners. And know: The moon has strong influence in this world only due to three aspects:
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of six types of lunar influence on earthly phenomena, presented as empirical observations. The text begins with a continuation of a list, likely from a preceding page. The first type discussed (though labeled 'third' in the text) concerns the humors in the human body. The author states that when the moon's light increases, the bodily humors increase, making the body appear more moist and handsome. Conversely, when the moon's light decreases, the humors retreat into the body and the body becomes drier. The third type (explicitly named) deals with medical crises: the variations in the states and days of crises are tied to the increase and decrease of the moon's light. The fourth type covers animal hair: its growth, thickness, and abundance correspond to the waxing moon, while waning slows and thins hair. Milk yield, brain size, and egg whites follow similar patterns. The author then notes that these conditions can vary within a single day depending on the moon's position: when the moon is in the eastern quadrant, milk and brains increase; when it sets, they decrease. These effects are confirmed by induction and are further supported by observations: people who sit or sleep in moonlight experience relaxation, laziness, catarrh, and headache; meat exposed to moonlight spoils. The fifth type concerns fish: during the first half of the month up to full moon, fish come out from depths and are fatter; after full moon, they retreat and lose fat. Within a day, fish emerge fatter when the moon is rising to the meridian. Similarly, insects emerge more in the first half of the month. The sixth type covers plants: trees planted during a waxing moon and when the moon is approaching the meridian grow stronger, multiply, and bear fruit; the opposite occurs during a waning moon and when the moon is away from the meridian. Aromatic plants, legumes, and herbs grow more during the first half of the month. Certain vegetables like gourds, cucumbers, and watermelons show perceptible growth differences within a single night around full moon. Minerals and springs also increase in the first half and decrease in the second half, as known to miners. The passage concludes with a statement that the moon has strong influence in this world due to three aspects, though the text breaks off before listing them.

Key Terms
القمر
الأخلاط
البحرانات
الاستقراء
الامتلاء
الاجتماع
الربع الشرقي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think these effects are superstitious or magical.
Correction: Al-Razi presents them as empirically observed natural regularities, not magical causation. He repeatedly invokes induction and gives specific examples to support his claims.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to fish in the second half of the lunar month?
A) They become fatter and more abundant.
B) They enter the depths and their fat decreases.
C) They remain at the surface and spawn.
D) They migrate to other waters.

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi's enumeration of lunar influences illustrates a pre-modern scientific approach that uses systematic observation and induction to argue for celestial-terrestrial causation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you truly observed the moon's phases and reflected on their consistent, detailed effects on your own body and surroundings? How does this neglect reveal a lack of deep engagement with the signs Allah has placed in your daily life? What are you missing by not paying attention?
?

If these subtle changes are real and designed by Allah, what does that say about the precision of His creation? And what does it say about your accountability to live in harmony with these natural rhythms? Are you ignoring the warnings your own body may be giving you through these signs?
?
The author states that sleeping in moonlight can cause discomfort and headache. How many times have you attributed such small ailments to chance, rather than considering that Allah may be speaking to you through natural causes? What would it take for you to become so attentive that you see His hand in every detail of your bodily and environmental changes?

beginner

Lunar Phases and Their Effects on Natural Entities
Details of lunar influence on fatness of animals, growth of plants, and yield of minerals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the author describes the influence of lunar phases on various natural entities, from animals to plants to minerals.

Core Idea
The moon's waxing and waning affect everything from animal fat to plant growth to mineral springs.

In this passage, the author presents empirical observations linking the moon's phases and its position in the sky to changes in animals, plants, and even minerals. This is not a theological argument but a naturalistic account that aligns with the broader Islamic tradition's recognition of celestial influences. Let's examine how the moon's cycle is said to impact various aspects of the natural world.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the full English translation. Let the author's own descriptions sink in.
Notice the repeated pattern of 'first half' vs 'second half' of the month.
2
Identify the entities and their patterns
List the different natural entities mentioned (animals, insects, trees, plants, cucurbits, minerals) and note how each is affected by the moon's phase.
The author uses specific terms like 'القمر زائد الضوء' (moon increasing in light) and 'ناقصاً في الضوء' (deficient in light).
3
Notice the consistent contrast
Observe that for almost every entity, the beneficial effects are associated with the first half of the month (waxing moon) and the opposite with the second half (waning moon).
The author even mentions that for cucumbers and watermelons, growth is so rapid that a difference is perceptible in a single night around full moon.
4
Reflect on the author's purpose
Consider why the author includes these details. Is he proving a theological point, or is he simply reporting observed natural phenomena?
The passage does not link these effects to divine causation explicitly; it is presented as empirical knowledge.

ويكون سمنها أزيد. وأما من بعد الامتلاء إلى الاجتماع فإنها تدخل في القعور وينقص سمنها. وأما في اليوم بليلته، فما دام القمر مقبلاً من المشرق إلى وسط السماء، فإنها تخرج سمينة، فإذا زال القمر عادت في أجحرتها، ولا تكون في غاية السمن. وكذلك أيضاً هوام الأرض يكون خروجها من أجحرتها في النصف الأول من الشهر، أكثر من خروجها في النصف الثاني. النوع السادس: إن الأشجار والغروس إذا غرست والقمر زائد الضوء ومقبل إلى وسط السماء: قويت وكثرت ونشأت وحملت النبات، وإن كان ناقصاً في الضوء زائلاً عن وسط السماء، كان بالضد، وكذا القول في الرياحين والبقول والأعشاب، فإنها تكون أزيد نشوءاً ونمواً إذا كان القمر من الاجتماع إلى الامتلاء. وأما في النصف الثاني من الشهر، فالحال بالضد من ذلك. والقرع والقثاء والخيار والبطيخ ينمو نمواً بالغاً عند ازدياد الضوء، فأما وسط الشهر عند فصول الامتلاء، فهناك يعظم النمو، حتى أنه يظهر التفاوت في الحس في الليلة الواحدة. وكذلك المعادن والينابيع. فإنها تزداد في النصف الأول من الشهر، وتنقص في النصف الثاني منه. وذلك معروف عند أصحاب المعادن.
And its fatness increases. And after fullness to conjunction, it enters in the holes and its fatness decreases. And in the day and its night, as long as the moon is advancing from the east to the middle of the sky, it comes out fat, and when the moon declines it returns to its holes, and it is not at the utmost fatness. And similarly also the creeping creatures of the earth: their coming out from their holes in the first half of the month is more than their coming out in the second half. The sixth type: that trees and saplings when planted while the moon is increasing in light and advancing to the middle of the sky: they become strong, abundant, and grow and bear vegetation; and if it is deficient in light and declining from the middle of the sky, the opposite occurs. And likewise the statement concerning basils, herbs, and grasses: they are more in growth and development when the moon is from conjunction to fullness. And in the second half of the month, the situation is opposite to that. And pumpkins, cucumbers, qiththa', and watermelons grow an extreme growth when light increases; and at the middle of the month at the times of fullness, growth becomes great, such that the difference is perceived by sensation in a single night. And likewise minerals and springs: they increase in the first half of the month and decrease in the second half. And that is known among the masters of minerals.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the moon's influence on various natural entities. It begins by discussing the fatness of an unspecified animal (likely one that lives in holes), noting how its fatness varies with the lunar cycle: after full moon until new moon, it becomes less fat; and during the day, as long as the moon is ascending in the sky, it comes out fat. Then it mentions that insects/reptiles come out of their holes more in the first half of the month. Then it presents the 'sixth type' concerning trees and saplings planted when the moon is waxing and ascending: they grow stronger and bear fruit; if waning and declining, weaker. Then it extends the same pattern to aromatic plants, herbs, and grasses. Then it gives examples of cucurbits that grow remarkably fast especially around full moon. Finally, it mentions minerals and springs increasing in the first half. The author notes that this is well-known among mineral experts. The passage does not provide a theological explanation but rather presents empirical observations consistent with the idea that the moon's phases and celestial position cause natural changes.

Three Reasons for the Moon's Powerful Influence
Gives three reasons why the moon has strong influence on this world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three specific reasons why the moon is considered to have a strong influence on the sublunar world according to this kalam argument.

Core Idea
The moon's influence comes from its speed, proximity, and light-mixing.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah presents a rational argument for the moon's special role in causing changes in this world. The author grounds the moon's influence on observable features: its rapid motion, its closeness, and its ability to blend planetary lights. As you read, notice how each reason builds on the previous one to establish the moon as the proximate cause of events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the literal translation. Let the author's argument structure come through.
Notice the three 'wujuh' (aspects) explicitly mentioned.
2
Identify each reason
Find the three reasons: speed of motion, proximity, and mixing of lights. For each, note the key phrase that supports it.
The author uses 'awla' (more appropriate) for the first two.
3

Reflect on why speed makes the moon more suitable for causing many changes, why proximity matters, and how light-mixing leads to being the proximate cause.
4
Consider the broader context
Think about how this argument fits into the larger discussion of planetary influence and causality in Islamic thought. Does it rely on observation or rational preference?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم: أن القمر إنما كان قوي التأثير في هذا العالم لثلاثة أوجه: أحدها: إن حركات القمر سريعة، وتغيرات هذا العالم كثيرة. وأما سائر الكواكب فحركتها بطيئة، وتغيرات هذا العالم كثيرة فكان إسناد تغيرات هذا العالم، مع كثرتها إلى حركات القمر أولى. والثاني: إنه أقرب الكواكب من هذا العالم، فكان بالتأثير فيه أولى. والثالث: إن القمر بسرعة حركاته، يمزج أنوار بعض الكواكب بأنوار الباقي. ولا شك أن امتزاجاتها، مبادىء لحدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم فكان القمر هو المبدأ القريب.
And know: that the moon has strong influence in this world due to three aspects: The first: that the motions of the moon are speedy, and the changes of this world are many. As for the rest of the planets, their motion is slow, and the changes of this world are many, so attributing the changes of this world, despite their abundance, to the motions of the moon is more appropriate. The second: that it is the closest of the planets to this world, so it is more appropriate for influence upon it. The third: that the moon, by the speed of its motions, mixes the lights of some planets with the lights of the rest. And there is no doubt that their mixtures are the beginnings for the occurrence of events in this world, so the moon is the proximate cause.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is an argument presenting three reasons why the moon has strong influence. It begins with a statement that the moon has strong influence for three aspects. First reason: the moon's motions are fast, and the changes in this world are many. Since other planets move slowly, it is more fitting to attribute the many changes to the fast-moving moon. Second reason: the moon is the closest planet, so it is most suitable to affect the earth. Third reason: the moon's rapid motion mixes the lights of other planets, and those mixtures are the origins of events, making the moon the proximate cause. The author uses 'أولى' meaning 'more appropriate' or 'more deserving'. The argument is based on efficiency and proximity.

Three Arguments for the Moon as Proximate Cause
The author enumerates three arguments for the moon as the proximate cause of sublunar changes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three reasons why classical Islamic cosmologists considered the moon the proximate cause of changes in the sublunar world.

Core Idea
The moon's speed, proximity, and light-mixing make it the immediate cause of earthly events.

This passage presents three distinct arguments that identify the moon as the proximate cause (المبدأ القريب) of changes in the world below. The author enumerates these reasons systematically, drawing on observations of planetary motion and light. As you read, note how each argument builds on a different physical property of the moon.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the enumeration markers (أحدها, والثاني, الثالث).
2
Identify each argument
List the three arguments: speed of movement, proximity, and mixing lights.
3
Reflect on 'proximate cause'
Consider the distinction between proximate and ultimate causes. The passage focuses on the immediate natural cause, not the ultimate divine cause.
The author does not deny ultimate causation by God.
4
Consider the underlying worldview
Think about how this fits into a broader causal framework where heavenly bodies influence earthly events.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحدها : إن حركات القمر سريعة ، وتغيرات [ هذا العالم كثيرة . وأما سائر الكواكب فحركتها بطيئة ، وتغيرات هذا العالم كثيرة ] فكان إسناد تغيرات هذا العالم، مع كثرتها [ إلى حركات (۳) ] القمر أولى . والثاني : إنه أقرب الكواكب من هذا العالم ، فكان بالتأثير فيه أولى . الثالث : إن القمر بسرعة حركاته ، يمزج أنوار بعض الكواكب بأنوار الباقي . ولا شك أن امتزاجاتها ، مبادىء لحدوث الحوادث في هذا العالم فكان القمر هو المبدأ القريب
First: The movements of the moon are fast, and the changes of this world are many. As for the other planets, their movement is slow, and the changes of this world are many, so attributing the changes of this world, with their multiplicity, to the movements of the moon is more appropriate. Second: It is the closest of the planets to this world, so it is more appropriate for affecting it. Third: The moon, due to its fast movements, mixes the lights of some planets with the lights of the rest. Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage presents three arguments—an enumeration—that the moon is the proximate cause (المبدأ القريب) of changes in the sublunar world. The first argument (أحدها) notes that the moon's movements are fast, while other planets move slowly; since the changes in this world are many, it is more fitting to attribute them to the moon's swift motions. The second argument (والثاني) points out that the moon is the closest planet to this world, so it is more suited to exert influence. The third argument (الثالث) explains that the moon, through its rapid motion, mixes the lights of various planets; these mixtures are undoubtedly principles (مبادىء) for the occurrence of events, making the moon the proximate cause. The author does not here discuss the ultimate cause (i.e., God), but focuses on the immediate astronomical cause.

The Enumeration of Celestial Movements and Their Purpose
Enumeration of celestial movements leading to infinite multiplicity, all ordered perfectly.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how celestial movements are enumerated from a finite count to an infinite multiplicity, and how all are coordinated to produce the perfect world system.

Core Idea
Infinite celestial motions are perfectly coordinated to produce the world system.

This passage from al-Matalib al-Aliyah presents a detailed count of celestial movements, starting with a base number and adding various types until the count becomes infinite. The author then highlights a profound truth: despite this overwhelming complexity, every movement is precisely arranged to bring about the most perfect order of the world. As you read, trace the progression of numbers and reflect on the harmony underlying apparent chaos.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse. Then read the translation. Notice how the author counts movements step by step.
Pay attention to the numbers: 42, 44, 45, then infinite.
2
Identify the types of movements
The passage mentions movements of the sphere of fixed stars, the highest sphere, representative spheres, carrying spheres, and epicycles. Identify each type and how it adds to the count.
3
Reflect on the purpose
The author concludes that all these movements result in the world system in the most correct and perfect way. Ask yourself: how does this show divine wisdom?
This connects to the overarching theme of causality and order.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحد من تلك السبعة فهي اثنان وأربعون حركة، وينضم إليها حركة فلك الثوابت بطبعه من المشرق إلى المغرب، وبالقسر على الضد فالمجموع أربعة وأربعون، وتنضم إليها الحركة البسيطة الحاصلة للفلك الأعظم، فيكون المجموع خمسة وأربعون نوعاً من الحركة. ثم إذا اعتبرنا أنواع الحركات الحاصلة بسبب حركات الأفلاك الممثلة والحاملة والتدويرات، كثرت الحركات جدا، فإذا امتزجت واختلطت بلغت تلك الكثرة إلى اللانهاية، وكلها واقعة على وجه يحصل بسببها نظام هذا العالم، على الوجه الأصوب الأكمل.
One from those seven becomes forty-two movements. There joins to it the movement of the sphere of fixed stars, by its nature from east to west, and by force in the opposite direction, so the total is forty-four. There joins to it the simple movement occurring for the highest sphere, so the total becomes forty-five types of movement. Then if we consider the types of movements occurring due to the movements of the representative spheres, the carrying spheres, and the epicycles, the movements become very numerous. When they mix and intermingle, that multiplicity reaches infinity, and all of them occur in a manner that results in the system of this world in the most correct and perfect way.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration of celestial movements. The author begins by stating that from each of seven (unspecified) categories comes forty-two movements. He then adds the movement of the sphere of fixed stars (both natural and forced) to reach forty-four, and then the simple movement of the highest sphere to reach forty-five. After considering the movements from representative spheres, carrying spheres, and epicycles, the number becomes infinite. Yet, despite this multiplicity, all movements are coordinated to produce the world system in the most perfect manner. The key point is the harmony underlying vast complexity.

The First Opinion on Sphere Speeds
The author states the first opinion on sphere speeds and notes the disagreement on fixed star motion rate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the well-known opinion regarding the speeds of celestial spheres and the controversy about the fixed stars' motion.

Core Idea
The highest sphere moves fastest, while the fixed stars move extremely slowly.

The author begins by presenting the first and most famous opinion about celestial movements. This opinion identifies the fastest sphere and explains the apparent motion of the fixed stars according to two different historical schools. Understanding this opinion sets the stage for the subsequent debate.

1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to grasp the opinion.
2
Identify the two spheres
Note the highest sphere and the fixed stars sphere and their relative speeds.
3
Compare the two rates
Notice the different rates of fixed star motion according to ancients vs later scholars.
4
Prepare for the controversy
Recognize that a discrepancy exists, leading to the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن عجائب أحوال هذه الحركات أن في حركات الأفلاك قولان. فالقول الأول وهو المشهور أن أسرع الكرات حركة هو الفلك الأعظم، فإنه يتحرك في اليوم والليلة على التقريب دورة تامة من المشرق إلى المغرب، وأما الفلك الذي حصل مماساً له في داخله وهو فلك الثوابت، فإنه يتحرك على مذهب المتقدمين في كل مائة سنة درجة واحدة، وعلى مذهب المتأخرين في كل ست وستين سنة درجة واحدة. ثم اختلفوا، فمنهم من قال هذا التفاوت إنما كان لأن المتقدمين غلطوا في الرصد، وأما المتأخرون فقد تنبهوا لذلك الغلط. ومن المحققين من قال نسبة هذا الغلط إلى المتقدمين كالبعيد جدا، وذلك لأن رصد عطارد كالمتعذر عند العقل، وذلك لأنه ليس له بعد كثير من الشمس البتة، وإنما يظهر أياما قلائل، وفي تلك الأيام فهو كوكب صغير الجرم، وليس له نور قاهر حتى يسهل ضبطه في آلات الرصد، فمع هذه الصعوبة التامة صارت أرصاد المتقدمين وافية بضبط حركاته ومعرفة أفلاكه، فلما لم يتفق لهم الغلط البتة في هذا المقام الصعب، فكيف يتفق لهم الغلط في حركات الكواكب الثابتة مع عظم أجرامها وقوة أنوارها؟ بل السبب في حصول هذا التفاوت أنه حصل فوق كرة الثوابت وتحت الفلك الأعظم كرة أخرى، وقطب فلك الثوابت منطبق على نقطة من تلك الكرة التي ذكرناها انطباقا، ليلزم من حركة هذه الكرات وصول قطب فلك الثوابت إلى حيث يصير منطبقا على قطب الفلك الأعظم، فلأجل هذه الحالة يصير مقدار الميل الأعظم متناقضا أبدا، وتصير حركات الثوابت أسرع في النظر والحس.
And among the wondrous aspects of these movements is that concerning the movements of the spheres there are two opinions. The first opinion, which is well-known, is that the fastest of the orbs in movement is the highest sphere, for it moves in a day and night approximately one complete revolution from east to west. As for the sphere that is tangent to it on its interior, which is the sphere of fixed stars, it moves according to the doctrine of the ancients one degree every hundred years, and according to the doctrine of the later scholars one degree every sixty-six years. Then they differed: some said this discrepancy is only because the ancients erred in observation, while the later scholars became aware of that error. But some investigators said that attributing this error to the ancients is extremely far-fetched, because the observation of Mercury is virtually impossible by reason, since it never has much distance from the sun, and it only appears for a few days, and during those days it is a small-bodied planet, and it does not have overpowering light to make it easy to fix in observational instruments. Yet despite this complete difficulty, the observations of the ancients were sufficient for recording its movements and knowing its spheres. Since they did not make any error in this difficult matter, how could they make an error in the movements of the fixed stars, given the greatness of their bodies and the strength of their lights? Rather, the cause of this discrepancy is that above the sphere of fixed stars and below the highest sphere there occurs another sphere, and the pole of the sphere of fixed stars coincides with a point of that sphere which we mentioned, so that from the movement of these spheres it necessarily follows that the pole of the sphere of fixed stars reaches a point where it comes to coincide with the pole of the highest sphere. Because of this state, the amount of the greatest inclination perpetually decreases, and the movements of the fixed stars become faster in sight and sensation.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the first opinion regarding celestial speeds and a refutation of the claim that ancient astronomers erred. It first states the opinion that the highest sphere is fastest, completing a daily rotation, while the fixed stars move extremely slowly (one degree per 100 or 66 years depending on the school). Some later scholars attributed the discrepancy to ancient errors in observation. The author strongly defends the ancients by pointing out that they accurately observed the difficult case of Mercury (which is small and close to the sun), so they could not have erred on the fixed stars which are large and bright. Instead, the author provides an alternative explanation: there exists an additional sphere between the fixed stars and the highest sphere. The pole of the fixed stars aligns with a point on that sphere, and due to the movement of these spheres, the pole of the fixed stars gradually aligns with the pole of the highest sphere, causing the fixed stars to appear to move faster over time. This resolves the discrepancy without accusing the ancients of error.
